ו</span><span dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span dir=LTR></span>,</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
which Greek covers somewhat artificially with </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>καὶ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐγένετο</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+
preposition + infinitive, or some other run-up to the main clause. Normal
English also does not have an expression like the Hebrew one.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>angel               </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>angel </i>as in supernatural messenger from God. As such, it refers to a
guardian angel for an individual (Matthew <b>18</b>:10?) or perhaps the church
in Revelation <b>1-3</b>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
evangelist</i> in </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Revelation <b>1</b>:20; <b>2</b>:1,
9, 12, 18; <b>3</b>:1, 7, 14. Apparently </span><u><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄγγελ</span></u><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>carries
the sense of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εὐ<u>αγγελ</u>ιστής</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and refers to the evangelist for the church or serves as an idealized term for
that work however many individuals were doing it. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>another</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (a)
not often used alone as a substantive. We have put a noun after it, as in <i>another
man.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
</i>The classical Greek distinction between </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἕτερος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄλλος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> does not hold very well in the New
Testament: <i>another in kind</i> (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἕτερος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
<i>vs.</i> <i>another in number</i> (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄλλος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
The new difference is <i>another viewed as distinct from</i> (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἕτερος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
<i>vs.</i> <i>another viewed as in relationship to </i>(</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄλλος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
In Galatians <b>1</b>:6-7, where both occur, we retained the classical
distinction: “<i>You’re turning away</i> <i>to</i> a different kind of [</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἕτερος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>]
<i>gospel</i> <i>that’s not really</i> another [</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄλλος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>]
<i>gospel at all</i>.”</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>answered</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         (a)
usually omitted from the full expression <i>answered and said</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
often omitted altogether after a question that the next sentence obviously
answers. As with dialog generally, the respondent’s words begin on a new line
without an introductory formula.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>anyone
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>anybody </i>as part of a general preference for –<i>body </i>indefinite
pronoun in place of –<i>one</i> indefinite relative</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>arise</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    often
omitted when it introduces an action and the actor is not actually seated or
lying down. It has the force of a Hebraism for ingressive action: Matthew <b>2</b>:7
(cp. 14); Mark <b>10</b>:1; <b>7</b>:24</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>as</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>        rendered
<i>like</i> for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὡς</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>καθώς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>as
a conjunction in keeping with modern usage. The traditional <i>as</i> in such
instances does not seem idiomatic: Luke<b> 22</b>:29; note examples in Hebrews:
<b>3</b>:8, 15; <b>4</b>:2, 3, 10; <b>5</b>:4;<b> 9</b>:25</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ass 
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     donkey</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>aught</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>authority</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
often replaced by <i>right</i> to present a more positive connotation</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
 style='text-decoration:none'>&nbsp;</span></span></u></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>baptize/baptism</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(a) used as loan words in most cases because they seem to label the act more
than its action </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>Immerse/immersion</i> appears where John’s baptism is linked to baptism in
the Holy Spirit: <i>“I’m immersing you in water, but he’ll ‘immerse’ you in the
Holy Spirit”</i> (Matthew <b>3</b>:11<sup>2</sup>; Mark <b>1</b>:8<sup>2</sup>;
Luke <b>3</b>:16<sup>2</sup>; John <b>1</b>:26, 33; Acts <b>1</b>:5<sup>2</sup>;
<b>11</b>:16<sup>2</sup>. Paul tells Timothy to <i>immerse</i> himself in the
use of his spiritual gift (1 Timothy <b>4</b>:15). It seemed advisable to use <i>immerse</i>
also in the account of Philip’s baptizing the Ethiopian eunuch, where the form
of the action is more evident (Acts <b>8</b>:38). Mark comments as well in 7:4
about the purification customs of the Jews and their immersing pots, <i>etc.</i>
<i>Wash</i> might have served in Mark <b>7</b>:4b if the writer is thinking of
these as lustrations.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
The baptism (of suffering) has the simple wording <i>baptism</i> instead of its
evident meaning <i>overwhelming by tribulation</i>: <sup>+</sup>[Matthew <b>20</b>:23
=], Mark <b>10</b>:38, 39; Luke <b>12</b>:50; 1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:29.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Bar-     Bar-
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>on
the front of names invariably means<i> son of. </i>Those names always appear
here without a hyphen, even though originally they may have been written with a
Maqqeph in Aramaic. They are evidently considered names rather than
descriptions because they stand by themselves—they are not add-ons to another
name. The exception here is Simon Barjonah in John <b>1</b>:42; <b>21</b>:15,
16, 17. The Greek text says </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Σίμον</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Ἰωάννου</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>Simon (son) of-John. </i>Matthew <b>17</b>:16 has </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Σίμων</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Βαριωνά</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.
The other cases are as follows:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Barabbas,
the insurrectionist: Matthew <b>17</b>:20, 21, 26; <b>27</b>:17; Mark <b>15</b>:7,
11, 15; Luke <b>23</b>:18; John <b>18</b>:40,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Barjesus,
the sorcerer: Acts <b>13</b>:6,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        Barnabas,
Paul’s companion missionary: Acts <b>5</b>:36, <i>etc.</i>,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        Barsabbas,
chosen as a possible replacement for Judas: Acts <b>1</b>:23,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        Bartholomew,
the apostle: Matthew <b>19</b>:3; Mark <b>3</b>:18; Luke<b> 6</b>:14; Acts <b>1</b>:13,</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        Bartimaeus:
Mark <b>10</b>:46</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        In
a related matter, <i>CV</i> has not used a comma after a name follow by <i>“son
of x”</i> as in <i>“x son of y.” </i>On the analogy of <i>Simon Barjonah</i>
(Matthew <b>16</b>:17) and <i>Timaeus Bartimaeus</i> (Mark <b>10</b>:46), the
supposition has been that the full set would have been considered the name in
most cases rather than a name plus a descriptive appositive: <i>Balaam son of
Beor</i> (2 Peter <b>2</b>:15); <i>James son of Alphaeus</i> (Matthew <b>10</b>:3;
Mark <b>3</b>:18; Luke <b>6</b>:15; Acts <b>1</b>:13<i>); James son of Zebedee</i>
(Matthew <b>10</b>:2); <i>John son of Zechariah</i> (Luke <b>3</b>:2); <i>Joseph
son of David</i> (Matthew <b>1</b>:20<i>);  Judas son of James</i> (Luke <b>6</b>:15;
Acts <b>1</b>:13); <i>Levi son of Alphaeus</i> (Mark 2:14); <i>Saul son of Kish</i>
(Acts <b>13</b>:21); <i>Sopater son of Pyrrhus </i>(Acts <b>20</b>:4); and <i>Zechariah
son of Berechiah</i> (Matthew <b>23</b>:35). One exception has been <i>Judas
son of Simon Iscariot</i> because of the longer appositive (John <b>15</b>:2). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>because</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
often dropped as a subordinating conjunction. In English a hearer naturally
takes the following clause as a reason for the preceding one when cause-effect,
purpose-result fits the context: Matthew <b>4</b>:17; Luke<b> 6</b>:20-21,
24-25; 1 Corinthians <b>2</b>:14; <b>3</b>:13.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>In
modern usage<i> because </i>has come to cover both subordinate and coordinate
values, previously <i>because</i> and<i> for</i>, respectively. When <i>because</i>
introduces a clause that is both short and subordinate, no comma appears: When
it introduces a long clause, a preceding comma usually does appear: If the <i>because
</i>is covering an illative value<i> </i>for <i>for</i>, a comma or semi-colon shows
that <i>because </i>has that value—or no conjunction is used at all: see
earlier note. Consistency on these points is challenging!</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>before</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
replaced with <i>in front of</i> when indicating position rather than time. A
positional use of <i>before</i> seems to appear less frequently in modern
English usage. <i>In front of</i> translates </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἔμπροσθεν</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐνώπιον</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐπί</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>πρό</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in positional usages. A hearer first
thinks of <i>before</i> as a time word, and then has to adjust to take it as a
position word when the sentence proceeds as a position statement.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>began</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
usually omitted because the New Testament has such a propensity for indicating
the beginning of an action. English usually omits making a point of that fact,
and lets the reader infer it. Note above the similarity with the use of <i>arise</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>beget/begat</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(a) <i>is/was father of</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                   
(b) <i>began in us</i> (1 Peter <b>1</b>:3)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>behold</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   always
omitted—along with <i>lo</i>; both translate </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἰδού</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ἴδε</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>interjections
generally have been omitted</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>believe             
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>in the name of him </i>shortened to “<i>believe <u>in</u> him”</i>: John<b>
1</b>:12; <b>3</b>:15, 16, 18;<b> 2</b>:23). <i>The name of</i> is Hebrew idiom
for noting identity, something not considered necessary in English. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>trust</i> <i>in
</i>often replaces <i>believe in</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>beloved</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    a
word falling out of use except in the traditional beginning of a wedding
ceremony; consequently, quite variously handled in <i>CV</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (a)
often <u>omitted</u> (Romans <b>16</b>; 5, 9; 1 Corinthians <b>10</b>:14; 2
Corinthians <b>6</b>:7; <b>12</b>:19; Philemon 12; 1 John <b>3</b>:2; <b>4</b>:11);
       </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<u>dearly loved</u> (Matthew <b>3</b>:17; Mark <b>1</b>:9; Luke <b>3</b>:22; Acts
<b>15</b>:25; Colossians <b>4</b>:14; 2 Peter <b>1</b>:17; Revelation <b>20</b>:9);
       </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<u>dear</u> (Mark <b>12</b>:6; Luke <b>20</b>:13; Ephesians <b>6</b>:21; <b>1</b>:6;
Colossians 1:7, 13; <b>4</b>:7, 9; 1 Thessalonians <b>2</b>:8; 2 Timothy<b> 1</b>:2;
Philemon 16; 2 Peter <b>3</b>:15)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<u>dear friend</u> (Jude 17);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(e)
<u>friend(s)</u> (Romans <b>9</b>:25; <b>16</b>:8; 2 Peter <b>3</b>:8; 2 Peter <b>3</b>:8,
14; 1 John <b>2</b>:7; <b>4</b>:1; Jude 3, 17); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (f)
close friend (Romans <b>16</b>:13);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (g)
<u>loved</u> (Romans <b>1</b>:7; 1 Timothy <b>6</b>:2; Philippians <b>4</b>:1;
Jude 1); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (h)
<u>highly regarded</u> (Romans <b>11</b>:28);  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (i)
I care about (1 Corinthians <b>4</b>:14);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (j)
he loves (Ephesians <b>5</b>:1); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (k)
I truly love (3 John 1);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (l)
dear fellow (servant) (Colossians<b> 1</b>:7)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>beware</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   expressed
as <i>watch out for</i> (the leaven of the Pharisees: Matthew <b>16</b>:6, 11;
Mark <b>8</b>:5; Luke <b>12</b>:1), <i>be careful </i>(Luke <b>8</b>:18; Acts <b>5</b>:35;
<b>13</b>:40)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>bishop</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>              (a)
<i>Bishop</i> appears twice to translate </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐπίσκοπος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Philippians
<b>1</b>:1; Titus <b>1</b>:7; the other uses are Acts <b>20</b>:28; 1 Timothy <b>3</b>:2;
1 Peter <b>2</b>:25<sup>+</sup>). We have retained it in Titus because it shows
that the New Testament uses </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐπίσκοπος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>and
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πρεσβύτερος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>interchangeably.
(Cp. also Acts <b>20</b>:17 + 28 for the synonymy of those terms, even though
we have used <i>oversee</i> in Acts <b>20</b>:28.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>overseer</i> in 1 Timothy<b> 3</b>:2; used once for Christ in 1 Peter <b>2</b>:25;
elsewhere a label for local leaders</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>blaspheme
      </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) reserved for slanderous speech toward deity </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i> insult,
rail out at, slander</i>, or equivalent expressions when directed at people</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>blessed</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (a)
<i>bless/blessed </i>used especially where one person is regarded favorably by
another; </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μακάριος</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>: Acts <b>3</b>:26;
<i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) replaced by <i>fortunate</i>
(</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>μακάριος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>). Paul before Agrippa, <i>“Í
consider myself </i>fortunate<i> to present my own defense”</i> (Acts <b>26</b>:2);
cp. <sup>+</sup>Matthew <b>5</b>:3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11; <b>13</b>:16;
Luke <b>6</b>:20<sup>2</sup>; <b>23</b>:29; Romans <b>4</b>:7, 8; <b>14</b>:22;
1 Peter <b>3</b>:14;<b> 4</b>:14; Revelation<b> 14</b>:13;<b> 19</b>:19.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>good
fortune</i> in Romans <b>4</b>:6, 9; James <b>1</b>:25; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:9</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>boat</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     the
term for a smaller craft as used on Lake Galilee; <i>ship </i>used for
sea-going vessels as on the Mediterranean.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>book
   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>book</i> in many places that could be talking about a scroll</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) replaced with <i>scroll</i> to
translate </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>βιβλίον</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in Revelation <b>5</b>:1,
2, 3, 7, 9, because John could tell that the <i>book</i> with seven seals had
writing inside and on the back. A codex would not necessarily show that. <i>Scroll</i>
appears also in Luke <b>4</b>:17-20 in connection with Jesus’ first rejection
at Nazareth.  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>brimstone</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
replaced by <i>sulfur</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>brother</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (a)
<u>omitted</u> if seemingly overused (Acts <b>15</b>:40; <b>21</b>:20; <b>22</b>:5;
Romans <b>1</b>:13; <b>7</b>:1, 4;<b> 8</b>:12; <b>16</b>:17; 1 Corinthians <b>1</b>:26;
<b>2</b>:1;<b> 4</b>:6; <b>7</b>:14, 29; <b>10</b>:1; <b>11</b>:33; <b>14</b>:6,
20, 39; <b>15</b>:50, 58; <b>16</b>:12; 2 Corinthians<b> 8</b>:1; Galatians<b>
3</b>:15; <b>4</b>:28; <b>5</b>:11;<b> 6</b>:1; Philippians<b> 1</b>:12; 1
Thessalonians<b> 4</b>:13;<b> 5</b>:4; Hebrews <b>3</b>:12; James <b>1</b>:2; <b>5</b>:7;
2 Peter <b>1</b>:20; <b>3</b>:17)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>as
a nod to inclusive speech, the following: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <u>brother
and/or sisters</u>: Matthew <b>18</b>:35; Romans <b>11</b>:15; <b>14</b>:13; <b>15</b>:14<sup>2</sup>;
1 Corinthians <b>1</b>:10; <b>3</b>:1; <b>12</b>:1; <b>14</b>:26; <b>15</b>:1,
50; <b>16</b>:16; 2 Corinthians <b>1</b>:8; <b>13</b>:11; Galatians <b>1</b>:2;
Philippians <b>3</b>:1; <b>4</b>:1, 21; Colossians<b> 4</b>:15; 2 Thessalonians
<b>2</b>:13; <b>3</b>:15; 2 Timothy <b>2</b>:14; James <b>2</b>:1; <b>4</b>:11;
<b>5</b>:19; 1 John<b> 1</b>:10; <b>3</b>:17</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
(fellow) <u>Christians</u>: Acts <b>11</b>:29; <b>14</b>:2; <b>15</b>:3, 33; <b>16</b>:2;
Romans <b>14</b>:10, 15; 1 Corinthians <b>5</b>:11;<b> 6</b>:1; <b>8</b>:11; 1
Thessalonians <b>3</b>:6; 1 John <b>3</b>:14, 16; <b>4</b>:20<sup>2; </sup></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<u>church</u>: Acts 16:40; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(e) <u>converts</u>:
Acts <b>15</b>:1, 32; <b>17</b>:6, 14; <b>18</b>:27; <b>21</b>:7; <b>28</b>:14,
15; Romans <b>16</b>:14; 1 Corinthians <b>13</b>:25; <b>16</b>:11, 20; 1
Timothy <b>4</b>:6; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(f) <u>disciples</u>:
Colossians<u> </u><b>1</b>:2; James <b>1</b>:9, 10; 3 John 10; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(g) <u>equals:</u>
1 Timothy <b>6</b>:2 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(h) <u>fellow
believers</u>: 1 Thessalonians <b>1</b>:10; <b>5</b>:26; 2 Thessalonians <b>4</b>:21;
Hebrews<b> 13</b>:1; 1 Peter <b>5</b>:9; 1 John <b>2</b>:9, 10; <b>3</b>:10; <b>5</b>:16;
3 John 5; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(i) <u>fellow Jews</u>:
Romans <b>9</b>:3<sup>2</sup>; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.25in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.25in'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(j)
friends: Matthew <b>25</b>:40; 2 Thessalonians <b>3</b>:15; Hebrews<b> 9</b>:11
&lt; Jeremiah <b>31</b>:34;  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(k) <u>r</u>eplaced
by <i>somebody else’s</i> (eye) (Matthew <b>7</b>:3; 1 Corinthians<b> 15</b>:1)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>but</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
<i> </i>Uncapitalized <i>but </i>between adversative clauses almost always has
a comma,<i> </i>even if the subject of the two clauses is the same. If the
value of <i>but </i>seems emphatic, capitalized <i>But</i> following a period is
used in place of the heavier, post-positive <i>however.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>can</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
In English, <i>can</i> has pretty well taken over the duties of <i>may</i> when
meaning <i>allow</i>: <i>“Yes, you can go.” May</i> applies to contingent
action: <i>“That may happen if you don’t take your medicine,”</i> a situation
where can often appears. Most English speakers no longer limit <i>can</i> to <i>be
able</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:12.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:
0in;margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
certain one(s)</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> traditionally used to translate the Greek
indefinite pronoun </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τις</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.
We have let the English indefinite article (<i>a/an</i>) suffice when the text
has a Greek singular </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τις</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, especially if
followed by a noun: <i>“He saw a certain poor widow”</i> becomes <i>“He saw a
poor widow”</i> (Luke <b>21</b>:2, <i>A certain</i> (<i>widow</i>) seems
redundant; <i>“certain” </i>can sound like the opposite of indefinite. In such
cases, the wording becomes <i>a </i>(<i>____</i>); note Luke <b>15</b>:11; <b>18</b>:2;
<b>23</b>:19. With plural </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τινες</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
we have reverted to <i>some</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>child/children</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(a) used only for immediate offspring, not for <i>descendants</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) limited as an
affectionate or familiar term; <i>guys</i> substitutes for it in John <b>21</b>:5;
sometimes replaced with <i>kids</i>: <sup>+</sup>Matthew <b>7</b>:11; <b>11</b>:16;
<b>15</b>:26; <b>19</b>:13, 14; <b>21</b>:15; Mark <b>7</b>:11, 28; <b>10</b>:13,
14, 15; Luke <b>7</b>:32; <b>11</b>:7, 13; <b>18</b>:16, 17; 1 Corinthians <b>13</b>:11;
1<b>4</b>:20; Ephesians <b>6</b>:4; 1 Thessalonians<b> 2</b>:7, 11  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>inhabitants</i>
of a city: Luke <b>19</b>:44 (Jerusalem)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Christ</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>              (a)
replaced by <i>Messiah</i> in the gospels and Acts <b>1-12</b>, which cover
mostly activities in the Jewish arena; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
kept generally as <i>Christ</i> in Acts <b>13-28</b>, the epistles, and
Revelation, which deal with the Gentile mission. As a reminder that <i>Christ</i>
is the same as <i>Messiah</i>, <i>Messiah</i> is added in superscript after the
first use of Christ in each epistle: Christ<sup>Messiah</sup>. Additionally, in
several places that seem to connect conceptually with the Messianic
anticipation, <i>CV</i> has arbitrarily added <i>Messiah </i>in superscript:
Romans<b> 5</b>:6, 8; <b>9</b>:3, 5; 1 Corinthians <b>10</b>:4; 2 Corinthians <b>3</b>:15;
Galatians <b>2</b>:21; <b>6</b>:12; Colossians <b>1</b>:20, 24; 1 John <b>2</b>:22;
5:1; Revelation<b> 11</b>:15; <b>12</b>:10. These are a few of the texts that
highlight the stick point in the Jews’ acceptance of Jesus as Messiah: that he
would suffer: Luke <b>24</b>:25-28; John <b>12</b>:34; Acts <b>2</b>:32-32.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>church
of God</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> (a) the expression used in lower case if apparently an
identity: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>1 Corinthians <b>1</b>:2;
<b>10</b>:32; <b>11</b>:22; <b>15</b>:9; 2 Corinthians<b> 1</b>:1 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) changed to <i>God’s
church</i> as a descriptor: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Acts
<b>20</b>:28; Galatians <b>1</b>:13; 1 Timothy <b>3</b>:5</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Circumcision</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  (a)
capitalized when designating Jews collectively more than describing them: <sup>+</sup>Acts
<b>10</b>:45; <b>11</b>:2; Romans <b>3</b>:30; <b>15</b>:8; Galatians <b>2</b>:9,
12; Philippians<b> 3</b>:2, 3; Colossians <b>4</b>:11; Titus <b>1</b>:10</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i> </i>in
lower case as a reference to the rite: Galatians <b>5</b>:6, 11; <b>6</b>:15;
Colossians <b>2</b>:11, 13, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>city                  </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
</i>reserved for the largest urban places that are called </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλεις</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Antioch, Athens, Bethlehem, Caesarea, Corinth. Damascus, Ephesus, Gaza, Gerasa,
Hebron, Philippi, Jericho, Jerusalem, Lysea, Rome, Samaria, Sidon, Tarsus,
Tyre. Because of uncertainty about the urban areas Paul and Barnabas went to on
their first tour, we used the expression <i>towns and cities</i> to translate </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλεις</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in
Act <b>15</b>:36: Salamis, Paphos, Antioch of Pisidia, Iconium, Lystra, Derbe.
We have kept <i>Bethlehem</i> as a “city” because of the familiar phrase <i>city
of David</i>, though it probably would not have qualified as a city from the
standpoint of size. The judgment call here is tentative because knowing the
population for ancient places is difficult. A number of New Testament locations
are not called </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>; so the issue is moot
for them.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Most other
places called </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλεις</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>we
have called <i>towns</i> as a reflection of our sense that they were not large.
<i>Village</i> translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κώμη</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>for
smaller country house groupings without public centers. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Basing the
rendering on supposed size contrasts with a more technical approach illustrated
by Bethsaida. In A.D. 30, Herod Philip upgraded the earlier village (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κώμη</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
into a city (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>) with certain features
of status as an administrative center in the Roman provincial structure. Mark <b>8</b>:22
calls it a (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κώμη</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>), Elsewhere it is called
a (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>): Matthew <b>11</b>:21 (&lt; <b>11</b>:20;
hence, <b>6</b>:45?); Luke<b> 9</b>:10; <b>10</b>:13; John in<b> 1</b>:44
(hence,<b> 12</b>:21?). Of course, the two systems of designation tend to
correspond.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>cock</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     <i>rooster</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>cold
(water)</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> weakened to <i>cool</i>; ancients around the
Mediterranean would not normally have had ice to make drinks “cold” in todays’
parlance: <sup>+</sup>Matthew <b>10</b>:42 (Luke<b> 16</b>:24).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>command(ment)</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
sometimes weakened to <i>tell</i> or <i>direct</i> when authority is not
prominent in the context</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>conceived 
 </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
by <i>became pregnant</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>conceived
and had a son</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    often shortened to <i>had a son</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>concerning
  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>about</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>confess</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (a)
<i>confess, </i>if guilt is involved, as is its modern implication (Mark <b>1</b>:5)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>agree</i>, <i>regard themselves as,</i> if agreeing with some fact, a
meaning that plays on the word picture in </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὁμολογέω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>to say the same thing</i>: “They <i>regarded themselves as</i> foreigners
and temporary residents on earth” (Hebrews <b>11</b>:13)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>acknowledge</i>
that, say, Jesus Christ is Lord: <i>“</i></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Everybody that<i> acknowledges
me </i>in front of people, I’ll <i>acknowledge </i>in front of my Father in
heaven<i>”</i> (Matthew <b>10</b>:32)<i>. </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>creature
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>created being</i>, as with the <i>living creatures</i> of Revelation <b>4</b>:6;
<b>5</b>:6, 8, 11, 14; <b>6</b>:1;<b> 7</b>:11; <b>14</b>:3;<b> 15</b>:7; <b>19</b>:4;
not used to mean <i>something created vs.</i> the creator. Modern usage
typically adds an unreal, abnormal connotation to the word. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>crowd</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
kept singular in most cases for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὄχλος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(used in the historical books) or </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>λαός</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>;
<i>people</i> as an alternative translation: John <b>7</b>:12, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>cry
(out)</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>          (a) covered by <i>shout</i>, as in John the
Baptist’s “shouting” in the desert (Matthew <b>3</b>:3; Mark <b>1</b>:3; Luke<b>
3</b>:4; John<b> 1</b>:15, 23)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>Cry</i> is reserved
for mourning, except for cases where people express obvious fear or when demons
<i>cry out</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>day</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      (a)
<i>day</i> for a twenty-four hour period</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (b)
<i>daylight</i> for when the sun shines</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:31.5pt;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (c) for indefinite time:
Luke <b>5</b>:35; <b>21</b>:6, 22; 1 Corinthians<b> 1</b>:14; Revelation <b>6</b>:17</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:31.5pt;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (d) <i>last day</i>
recast as <i>in the end </i>(John <b>6</b>:40, 54; <b>11</b>:24)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:31.5pt;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (e) NOTE on John <b>2</b>:1:
John traces a series of days in <b>1</b>:19-28, <b>1</b>:29 (<i>“the next day”</i>),
<b>1</b>:35 (<i>“the next day”</i>), <b>1</b>:43 (<i>“the next day”</i>), and
then <b>2</b>:1 says <i>“on the third day.”</i> <i>CV</i> has taken <i>“the
third day”</i> as after the immediately previous “morrow/next day” (<b>1</b>:43)
rather than as a third day in sequence with the immediately preceding two “next
days” in <b>1</b>:35 and 43. (a)The location of Bethany (Bethabara?) beyond the
Jordan River is unknown, but of the minimum five days in <b>1</b>:19-<b>2</b>:1,
the middle day seems still to be at Bethany because in <b>1</b>:43 Jesus has
not left for Galilee. It might be a stretch to walk from Bethany to Cana in two/three
days while stopping by Nazareth with Peter, Andrew, Phillip, and Nathaniel on
the way (<b>2</b>:2), maybe fifty miles as the crow flies. (b) There are four
preceding days enumerated, not just two; <i>“third day”</i> does not sequence
after four. It seems less likely to take only two of those four in speaking of
a <i>“third day”</i> for <b>2</b>:1. (c) A Sabbath may be included as well in
the final set of three days as envisioned by this reconstruction. So the
translation of <b>2</b>:1 becomes <i>“three days later,” </i>that is, <i>“the
third day”</i> after the previous <i>“next day.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>debts</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    not
used for <i>sins</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(the)
deep</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
called <i>open water</i> (2 Corinthians <b>11</b>:25) or <i>deep water</i>
(Luke <b>5</b>:4). Elsewhere deep when used as an adjective: Acts <b>20</b>:9;
Romans <b>8</b>:9; 2 Corinthians <b>8</b>:2; Ephesians <b>5</b>:32; Colossians <b>4</b>:13;
Revelation <b>2</b>:24.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>demon</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
one involved in “demon possession.” <i>It</i> serves as the pronoun for demons.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>deny</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
<i>deny</i> if referring to a fact</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>deny who ____ is</i> if
referring to an identity: “</span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Whoever denies </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>who
I am<i> in front of people, I’ll deny </i>as belonging to me <i>in front of my
Father in heaven”</i> (Matthew<b> 10</b>:33)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>desert</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  (a)
<i>desert</i> for an inhospitable place</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>open country </i>for an
unpopulated, sparsely populated, or remote area as “deserted of people</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>devil</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    only
as a reference to Satan; there are many demons but one devil</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>disbelieve/disbelief/disbeliever</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
used instead of <i><u>un</u>belief</i> because <i>unbelief</i> could mean not
believing because of not hearing: <b><sup>+</sup></b>Mark <b>6</b>:6; [[<b>16</b>:16]];
Luke <b>12</b>:46; John <b>3</b>:18; 2 Corinthians <b>4</b>:4; <b>6</b>:15; 2
Thessalonians <b>2</b>:12; 1 Timothy<b> 1</b>:13; Hebrews <b>3</b>:18, 19; <b>4</b>:6;
1 Peter<b> 2</b>:7; <b>4</b>:17</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>drink</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    usually
omitted in the expression <i>eat and drink</i>: Matthew <b>6</b>:25; 1
Corinthians <b>9</b>:4; <b>11</b>:22. In English, <i>eating</i> includes
whatever is part of the meal</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>dumb   </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not
used, so never used to mean <i>mute</i>, that is, as designating someone who
cannot speak</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>edify</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
dropped in favor of <i>help</i> (Even though it is not a close equivalent, it
is a more everyday term): <b><sup>+</sup></b>Romans <b>14</b>:19; 1 Corinthians
<b>10</b>:23; <b>14</b>:3<sup>3</sup>, 5, 12, 17, 26; 2 Corinthians <b>12</b>:19</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(the)
elect</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> replaced by <i>chosen ones/people</i>; <i>the elect</i>
may not be clear to people not acquainted with its specialized usage in
Christianity: Matthew <b>24</b>:22, 24, 31; Mark <b>13</b>:20, 22, 27; Luke <b>18</b>:7;
Romans <b>11</b>:7; 1 Peter <b>1</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>election</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     <i>choice</i>
or <i>divine choice</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>empire</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
the translation for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οἰκουμένη</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
<b><sup>+</sup></b>Luke <b>2</b>:1; Acts <b>11</b>:28; <b>17</b>:6; <b>24</b>:5;
see also <i>world </i>below.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>every 
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  Contemporary
usage often makes <i>every</i> and its cognates distributive plurals as shown
by the plural pronouns sometimes used to refer back to them. </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>CV</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
has allowed that idiom in a few places like James <b>1</b>:5, <i>“If you need
wisdom, ask God. He gives it generously to <u>everybody</u> without </i></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>blaming
<u>them</u> for asking<i>.”</i> Cp. Luke <b>4</b>:20, <i>“<u>Everybody</u> in
the synagogue gave him <u>their</u> full attention.”</i> Romans <b>13</b>:7, </span><b><i><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“</span></sup></i></b><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Pay
everybody what’s due them.”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> See also Revelation<b> 13</b>:16.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Every</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
like </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>all,</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
indicates a significant number rather than an absolute number. In Mark <b>1</b>:5,
for example, </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>CV</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> has said </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>the
people</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> instead of everyone went out to have John baptize
them. The religious leaders certainly did not.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>evil
                 </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>In the model prayer (Matthew <b>6</b>:9-13),
we have said <i>“deliver us from the evil one</i> [</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐκ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τοῦ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πονηροῦ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>],”
rather than <i>“from evil.”</i> This first alternative takes it as a masculine
substantive on the analogy of Matthew <b>13</b>:19, <i>“the evil one comes and
snatches it away”</i>; note also <i>the evil one </i>in Matthew <b>5</b>:37; <b>13</b>:38;
John <b>17</b>:15; Ephesians <b>6</b>:16 (<i>“the flaming arrows from the evil
one”</i>), 2 Thessalonians<b> 3</b>:3.  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>1 John <b>5</b>:18-20
makes it clear that the phrase means <i>“the evil one” </i>rather the <i>“evil,”</i>
because the texts goes on to say that the whole world lies in <i>“the evil
one.” </i>We would not expect the text to say that the whole world lies in <i>“evil.”</i>
Besides, the passage goes on to contrast the world with us who lie in <i>“the
true one.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>An alternative
takes the genitive singular as a neuter substantive on the analogy of Matthew <b>5</b>:11,
<i>“say all (kinds of) evil-things about you.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>CV<i>
</i>has often substituted words like<i> bad </i>and <i>sinful </i>for <i>evil</i>
because the latter seems too strong. <i>Bad</i> may be too weak, and <i>sinful</i>
is too narrow. <i>Sinful</i> has more to do with behavior whereas <i>evil</i>
can cover undesirable circumstances that come to the sinner. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>eyes                 </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>eyes</i> when indicating the organ for sight</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>eyelids</i> where Jesus <i>“touched the eyes”</i> in healing blindness: <b><sup>+</sup></b>John
<b>9</b>:6, 11, 15 (the man born blind), Matthew <b>9</b>:28 (two blind men),
Matthew <b>20</b>:34 (two blind men at Jericho)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<i>“in the eyes of,”</i> an example of body-part speaking, usually replaced
with a circumlocution if indicating someone’s way of looking at
something/someone; similarly, <i>“open the eyes of”</i> (caused to see as with
the man born blind in John <b>9</b>:30); <i>“eye fell on”</i>; <i>“lifted up
the eyes”</i> (for <i>“looked”</i>) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>faith</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                 (a)
<i>Faith</i> translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πίστις</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
as in Hebrews <b>11</b>, where the term’s broad meaning applies as seen by how the
Hebrew writer describes the faithful ones he cites.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>Trust</i>
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πίστις</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in
salvation contexts of (Romans, Galatians, and in some other places). Paul’s
point is that the decisive act in salvation lies in divine choice rather than
in human effort (whether formal, interpersonal, or behavioral). His reasoning
rests on Habakkuk <b>2</b>:4 and its terminology. As in all cases of renewing
broken interpersonal relationships, the one “saved” from the alienation
