(lostness) can only “trust” the other to forgive and receive back into the
relationship (reconciliation). In that light, our translation of Habakkuk <b>2</b>:4
as worded in Romans <b>1</b>:17 and Galatians <b>3</b>:11 is, <i>“A good person
will have life by trusting.”</i> Hebrews <b>10</b>:38 reads, <i>“My good person
will have life by faith,” </i>because the Hebrew writer applies it broadly
throughout the upcoming examples in chapter<b> 11</b>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>Believe</i>
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πίστις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> when information more
than relationship is the topic. James <b>2</b>:14-26 demonstrates this usage of
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πίστις</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πιστεύω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
something even demons do. We believe ideas; we trust persons.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d) We have
considered <i>believe in </i>as a verb-form construction equal to <i>faith </i>as
<i>trust</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>fall
down  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>in some cases replaced with kneel down: Matthew <b>9</b>;
Mark <b>3</b>:4; Revelation <b>4</b>:10; <b>5</b>:8, 14; <b>19</b>:4</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>father(s)</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>          (a)
reserved for a parent </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) sometimes
replaced by <i>dad</i>: <sup>+</sup>Mark <b>9</b>:21, 24; Luke <b>9</b>:42; <b>15</b>:21;
John <b>4</b>:53; Ephesians <b>6</b>:4; Colossians <b>3</b>:21</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) not used for <i>ancestors</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>See
the entry for <i>sons</i>, a correlative term with <i>father</i>; that is, the
range of applications for one word corresponds to the range of usages for the
other.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>fear</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                  (a)
<i>fear</i> in the normal sense</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) covered by
less extreme terms like <i>respect</i> (Acts <b>9</b>:31) or <i>take heed</i>
(1 Tomothy <b>5</b>:20). Like <i>hate</i> and <i>rule</i>, the word </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>φόβος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>covers
a wider range of degrees than the English <i>fear</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>fear
and trembling</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (a) The expression seems too extreme in
some examples: 1 Corinthians <b>2</b>:3; 2 Corinthians <b>7</b>:15; Ephesians <b>6</b>:5;
Philippians<b> 2</b>:12.             </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) perhaps a
hendiadys: <i>trembling fear</i>, as in <i>“felt fear”</i> <i>vs.</i> mental
apprehension.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>See also comments
on “double entry” herein.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Feast  
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>entered
as <i>festival </i>when speaking of the stated Jewish “feasts,”<i> </i>especially
in John’s gospel: Matthew <b>26</b>:5; <b>27</b>:15; Mark <b>14</b>:1, 2; <b>15</b>:6;
Luke <b>2</b>:41, 42; <b>22</b>:1; John <b>4</b>:45;<b> 5</b>:1; <b>6</b>:4; <b>7</b>:2,
8, 11, 14, 37:<b> 10</b>:22; <b>11</b>:56;<b> 12</b>:12, 20; <b>13</b>:1, 29;
Colossians <b>2</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(at
the) feet (of) __ </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The phrase is an example of Hebrew’s
body-parts idiom. It implies subordination to the person named. We have largely
avoided the expression, saying instead </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>that Jairus came
and knelt <i>in front of</i> Jesus (Mark <b>5</b>:22);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>that the healed
demoniac was <i>sitting by</i> Jesus (Luke<b> 8</b>:35); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Mary fell down to
Jesus (John <b>11</b>:32<sup>ms</sup>);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>that Paul <i>studied
under</i> Gamaliel (Acts <b>22</b>:3); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            that God <i>subjected</i>
everything to Christ (1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:27). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>flee      </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sometimes
replaced by<i> run away</i>, <i>escape</i>, <i>get away from</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>flesh</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    English
seldom speaks of </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>flesh</span></i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in the sense of </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“meat</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,</span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>”</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> except
perhaps in medical circumstances. Finding alternatives for the frequent use of
the word (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σάρξ</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>) has proved difficult. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)</span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> Physical</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
sometimes works: John <b>1</b>:13, 14; <b>3</b>:2</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>2</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>;
Romans <b>1</b>:3-5;<b> 9</b>:3, 5; <b>9</b>:8; <b>13</b>:14, </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>etc.</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Physical</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
also covers for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σαρκινός</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Romans
<b>7</b>:14) and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σαρκικός</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Romans
<b>15</b>:27). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Flesh
and blood</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>other people</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(in contrast to God) as in Jesus’ observation about Peter’s Good Confession
(Matthew <b>16</b>:17). See also Galatians <b>1</b>:16; Ephesians <b>6</b>:12.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)
</span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>In
the flesh</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> falls out altogether when Paul speaks of </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“your
masters according to the flesh”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (Ephesians<b> 6</b>:5).
His reference seems clear enough without the added phrase.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>NOTE:
Finding a replacement for “flesh” is especially difficult because Paul uses
that “body-part” term as a code word for self-centered living (Romans<b> 8</b>:1-19).
To satisfy the “flesh,” something must be taken into it. The words </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>body</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>meat</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> do
not usually function well in that regard. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d) We have
rendered it </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“body” </span></i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in Ephesians <b>5</b>:29.
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>follow
me</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
<i>come (on) with me</i> as in the calling of various disciples: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>4</b>:19; <b>8</b>:22; <b>9</b>:9; <b>19</b>:21; Mark <b>1</b>:17; <b>2</b>:14;
<b>10</b>:21; Luke <b>5</b>:27; <b>9</b>:59; <b>18</b>:22; John<b> 1</b>:43.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>for     
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>used
only as a preposition: “<i>for</i> the Lord”; not as a conjunction </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>English has lost
the <i>for-because</i> distinction. <i>For</i> falls out, and <i>because</i>
serves as coordinating conjunction (<i>for</i>) and subordinating conjunction (<i>because</i>).
That is one reason writers have to think whether to insert a comma ahead of <i>because</i>,
which is done especially when it has coordinate conjunctive value.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            Besides, the Greek word </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γάρ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(<i>for</i>)
often carries an illative sense rather than a logical or causal sequence. The
wording after <i>for</i> expands on the previous point rather than giving a
reason or cause for it. Aside from translating classical works, English does
not use <i>for</i> as illative; it is reserved for use as a preposition: <i>“He
did it <u>for</u> me.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            Beyond these points lies
the English tendency to omit altogether any word for the causal connection
between two statements, coordinate or subordinate. The listener makes the
connection automatically for contextual reasons; hence, <u>for</u> and <u>because</u>
end up being omitted.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>forever</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εἰς</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τοὺς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>αἰῶνας</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>to the ages</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>forevermore</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εἰς</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τοὺς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>αἰῶνας</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τῶν</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>αἰώνων</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>to the ages of the ages </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(for
the) forgiveness of sins  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John’s <i>“baptism of repentance <u>to
forgive</u> sins”</i>: Mark <b>1</b>:4; Luke <b>3</b>:3; without the added
prepositional phrase (Acts <b>13</b>:24). Note also Christ’s blood <i>“shed for
remission/forgiveness of sins”</i> (Matthew <b>26</b>:28); <i>“baptism to</i>
[identity with] <i>Christ </i>[identity with whom serves as the basis] <i>for
the forgiveness of sins”</i> (Acts<b> 2</b>:38; cp. <b>8</b>:16; <b>19</b>:5;
Romans <b>6</b>:3; Galatians <b>3</b>:27) in contrast to <i>“baptized to Paul” </i>(1
Corinthians <b>1</b>:13, 15), <i>“baptized to Moses”</i> (1 Corinthians <b>10</b>:2);
<i>“baptized to repentance”</i> (Acts <b>19</b>:4).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>foundation</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
<i>founding</i> as in the <i>founding of the world</i>: Matthew <b>13</b>:35; <b>25</b>:34;
Luke <b>11</b>:50; John <b>17</b>:24 (<i>“before the world existed”</i>);
Ephesians <b>1</b>:4 (<i>“founded the world”</i>); Hebrews<b> 1</b>:10 (<i>“founded
the earth”</i>);<b> 4</b>:3 (<i>“founded the world</i>”); <b>9</b>:26 (<i>“since
the world began”</i>); 1 Peter <b>1</b>:20; Revelation <b>13</b>:8; <b>17</b>:8.
English uses <i>foundation</i> for the basis of a structure or what a
foundation can serve to represent. Foundation as <i>the act of founding</i> has
fallen out of English usage.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>fruit
    </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
used only for what trees produce or some plant item that is sweet (There is a
more technical use, but we have dispensed with that usage.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>grain</i>, <i>produce</i>, <i>result</i>
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>descendant</i>, <i>offspring</i>,
<i>your baby</i> translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>καρπός</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
in other situations (Luke<b> 1</b>:42; Acts <b>2</b>:30)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>fulfill</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                (a)
<i>fulfill</i> as the accomplishment of a prediction </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Fulfill</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
is a correlative term with <i>prophesy</i>; that is, the range of meanings for
the one matches the range of meanings for the other. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Matthew <b>2</b>:23
says <i>Nazareth</i> fulfills Isaiah’s prophecy about a “shoot” that comes out of
Jesse (</span><i><span style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>nezer</span></i><span
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, shoot [</span><span lang=HE
dir=RTL style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>נצר</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span dir=LTR></span>]</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>;
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Isaiah<b>
11</b>:1; <b>53</b>:2). The connection evidently lies in the sound of the word
for “shoot” in the Messianic prediction. So we have rendered it <i>reminds us
of</i>. We have supposed that Matthew does not intend to claim that Jesus’
living in Nazareth directly fulfilled an Old Testament prediction; it was a
fitting fact.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)
Matthew <b>2</b>:15 cites Hosea <b>11</b>:1, “<i>I</i></span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>’</span></i><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ve
called my son </span></i><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>o</span></i><i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ut of Egypt.” </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>But
<i>son</i> refers to Israel, not to Israel’s Messiah. The connection lies in
the fact that God constituted Israel—of whom Messiah was the future leader—as a
separate nation, rather than a subunit under Egypt. We have rendered it <i>in
keeping with</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
Matthew <b>13</b>:14 we have supposed <i>illustrates</i> Isaiah’s more general
description of Israelites as <i>“hearing but not comprehending,”</i> <i>etc.</i>
(Isaiah <b>6</b>:9-10). The passage appears not to reference Jesus’ immediate
audience particularly (cp. Mark <b>4</b>:12; Luke <b>8</b>:10; John <b>12</b>:40;
Acts<b> 28</b>:26-27; as well as Romans <b>10</b>:16; <b>11</b>:8). If applied
in multiple situations, the Isaianic text is not a specific prediction of any
one of them</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        So
the similar uses of <i>fulfill</i>—as not meaning fulfilling a specific
prediction, but as a class reference applied to this situation—in Matthew <b>8</b>:17;
<b>13</b>:35 are translated accordingly.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>generation       
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>people today</i> (Luke <b>7</b>:8-35), <i>at this time</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                         </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>their own kind</i> (Luke <b>16</b>:8)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Gentiles</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
In the New Testament, <i>Gentiles</i> regularly refers to non-Jews. It is
something of a specialization of the Hebrew word for <i>nations</i> in the Old
Testament. Only in New Testament citations of Old Testament texts where <i>nations</i>
occurs does <i>Gentiles</i> show up as the Old Testament translation of </span><span
lang=HE dir=RTL style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>גוֹי</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span> (to show OT-NT connection): Deuteronomy <b>32</b>:43; Psalm <b>2</b>:1;
<b>18</b>:49; <b>117</b>:1; Isaiah <b>9</b>:1; <b>11</b>:10; <b>42</b>:1, <b>49</b>:6;
Amos <b>9</b>:12. If <i>nations</i> does not contrast with Jews, it can carry
it elemental meaning; otherwise <i>Gentiles</i> is its natural translation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>give</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     (a)
frequently <i>give</i> in the normal sense</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>allow</i>: To <i>give someone
to do something</i> means to <i>let</i> them to do it: John <b>3</b>:27; <b>6</b>:65;
<b>10</b>:11; Acts <b>13</b>:35. As such it follows the usages of the Hebrew </span><span
lang=HE dir=RTL style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>נתן</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)<i>
offer</i>, <i>make available</i> (Acts <b>11</b>:18)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>glory</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
sometimes <i>brightness</i> (Acts<b> 22</b>:11)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>give credit to</i> (Acts <b>12</b>:23)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (c) <i>honor
</i>covers instances where <i>glory</i> seems too extreme or foreign for
current usage of the English term: Luke <b>2</b>:32; John <b>7</b>:18; Romans <b>9</b>:4,
23, 24; <b>15</b>:7; 1 Corinthians <b>2</b>:7; <b>10</b>:31; <b>15</b>:43; 2
Corinthians <b>1</b>:20;<b> 8</b>:19, 23; Philippians <b>3</b>:19; 1
Thessalonians <b>2</b>:6, 12, 19; 2 Thessalonians <b>2</b>:14; Hebrews <b>3</b>:3;
2 Peter 1:3; Revelation <b>14</b>:7. <i>Honor</i> could not be substituted in
passages that also gave the regular word for honor (</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τιμή</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Romans<b> 2</b>:7; 1 Timothy <b>1</b>:17, <i>etc</i>.). <i>Glory </i>was kept
in places that applied it to God.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>go</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>        (a)
used only for traveling</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) sometimes omitted as an
ingressive marker: <i>“(Go) tell that old fox”</i> (Luke <b>13</b>:32)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>“go __” </i>retained
especially if movement is involved: Matthew <b>5</b>:24; <b>8</b>:21;<b> 9</b>:13;
<b>13</b>:28; <b>18</b>:15; <b>19</b>:21; <b>21</b>:28; <b>28</b>:10, 19; Mark <b>6</b>:37,
38; <b>16</b>:7</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Go
in peace</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>   replaced with <i>“Have a good day”</i> (Mark <b>6</b>:34;
Luke <b>7</b>:50; <b>8</b>:48; Acts <b>16</b>:56), hardly having the same
quality, but more akin to what we would say.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>God                 </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
capitalized in reference to the <u>Father</u> (or perhaps to the Godhead)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
lower case for <u>pagan deities</u> (Acts <b>17</b>:18; 1 Corinthians <b>8</b>:5;
Acts<b> 7</b>:40; <b>14</b>:11; <b>17</b>:18; Galatians<b> 4</b>:8), </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>idols</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
used to represent them (Acts 1<b>9</b>:26<sup>2</sup>; 1 Corinthians <b>8</b>:5),
and </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>leaders</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
under God (John <b>10</b>:34, 35 &lt; Psalm <b>82</b>:6)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
translated <i>deity</i> in passages where </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>θεός</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>seems
not to refer to God as an individual but to deity as a kind of being: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John
<b>1</b>:1, 18; <b>5</b>:18; <b>10</b>:33; Acts <b>17</b>:29; Philippians<b> 2</b>:6;
Colossians <b>2</b>:9; 2 Thessalonians <b>2</b>:4<sup>2</sup>; 1 John<b> 5</b>:20.
Our assumption has been that such passages used </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>θεός</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
as the noun equivalent of the adjective </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>θεῖος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>divine/deific</i>. As such, it is a synonym for the <i>hapax legomenon</i> </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>θειότης</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(Romans <b>1</b>:20).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>God-fearer</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      (a)
the translation for four times in Acts where Luke uses </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σεβόμενος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
to designate a believer in God not officially joined to Judaism as by
circumcision: <b>16</b>:14 (Lydia); <b>17</b>:4, 17; <b>18</b>:7 (Titus). The
specialized term is a substantive participle that comes from a verb meaning <i>to
worship</i>; hence, a <i>worshiping one</i>, <i>devout one, godly one</i>. As a
participle modifier, it describes <i>devout</i> proselytes (<b>13</b>:43) and
women in Antioch of Pisidia (<b>13</b>:50). The full verb </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σεβέομαι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
translates <i>to worship</i> in <b>18</b>:13 (God) and <b>19</b>:27 (Artemis)
as well as in two quotations of Isaiah <b>39</b>:13 (Matthew <b>15</b>:9 = Mark
<b>7</b>:7). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
the translation for four times in Acts where Luke uses the phrase </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>φωβούμενοι</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τὸν</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>θεόν</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(<i>“the
ones fearing God”</i>), which we have taken as a semantic equivalent to the
other expression: <b>10</b>:1, 22 (Cornelius); <b>13</b>:16, 26.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>God
forbid</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> replaced with <i>“goodness, no”</i> to translate </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μὴ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γένοιτο</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
literally, <i>it ought not be</i>: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>20</b>:16; Romans<b> 3</b>:4, 6, 31; <b>6</b>:2, 15; <b>7</b>:7, 13; <b>9</b>:14;
<b>11</b>:1, 11; 1 Corinthians <b>6</b>:15; Galatians <b>2</b>:17;<b> 3</b>:21.
Equals the <i>God forbid </i>in older translations</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>gospel</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>       
<i>gospel</i> or <i>message</i> when </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εὐαγγέλιον</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>εὐαγγελίζομαι</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> are a <u>label</u> for
the Christian message, and<i> good news</i> when </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εὐαγγέλιον</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
highlights <u>content</u>. The passages involved are Matthew<b> 4</b>:23; <b>9</b>:35;
<b>11</b>:5; <b>24</b>:14; <b>26</b>:13; Mark <b>1</b>:14, 15; <b>8</b>:35; <b>13</b>:10;
<b>14</b>:9; [[<b>16</b>:15, 20]]; Luke <b>1</b>:19; <b>2</b>:10; <b>3</b>:18; <b>4</b>:18;
<b>7</b>:22; Acts <b>8</b>:25, 35, 40; <b>10</b>:36; <b>13</b>:32; <b>14</b>:7,
14, 21; <b>15</b>:7; <b>20</b>:24; Romans<b> 1</b>:1, 9, 16;<b> 2</b>:16; <b>10</b>:16;<b>
11</b>:28; <b> 15</b>:16, 19; <b>16</b>:25; 1 Corinthians <b>1</b>:17; <b>4</b>:15;
<b>9</b>:12, 14, 16, 18, 23; <b>15</b>:1; 2 Corinthians <b>2</b>:12; <b>4</b>:3,
4; <b>9</b>:13; <b>10</b>:14, 16; <b>11</b>:7; <i> </i>Galatians <b>2</b>:5, 7;
<b>3</b>:8; <b>4</b>:13; Ephesians <b>1</b>:13; <b>3</b>:6; <b>6</b>:15, 19;
Philippians<b> 1</b>:12, 16, 27<sup>2</sup>; <b>2</b>:22;<b> 4</b>:15;
Colossians <b>1</b>:23; 1 Thessalonians <b>1</b>:5; <b>2</b>:2, 4, 8, 9; <b>3</b>:2,
6; 2 Thessalonians<b> 1</b>:8; <b>2</b>:14; 1 Timothy <b>1</b>:11<sup>2</sup>;
2 Timothy <b>1</b>:8, 10; <b>2</b>:8; Philemon 13; Hebrews <b>4</b>:2, 6; 1
Peter <b>4</b>:6, 17; Revelation <b>14</b>:6, and other texts. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>In Galatians<b> 1</b>:6-12 we
retained <i>gospel</i> throughout; <i>another kind of “good news”</i> would not
fit the situation very well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>grave</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>               (a)
<i>grave </i>for a burial place dug in the ground (</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ταφή</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τάφος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>);
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i> tomb</i>
for an erected burial chamber or one hewn into a hillside (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μνημεῖον</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
Luke <b>11</b>:47); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Sepulcher</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>crypt</i>, <i>vault</i>, and <i>burial chamber</i> are not used.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>great
   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
</i>used only for quality, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) not used for size (except
Revelation <b>20</b>:11); replaced by <i>big</i>, <i>large</i>, <i>huge</i>,
even <i>tremendous</i> to describe the big herd of 2,000 pigs (Matthew <b>8</b>:30
and parallels)!</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>greet/salute</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
reduced in number in Paul’s lengthy set of salutations in Romans <b>16</b>:1-24
and Colossians <b>4</b>:7-17.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>hand</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                (a)
regularly <i>hand</i> as the meaning of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>χείρ</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
In the context of Christ’s crucifixion, we have used <i>wrist</i>, supposing
that the spikes were likely driven between the ulna and the radius there (John <b>20</b>:25,
26). That manner of driving the spike would also be less likely to break a
“bone,” which texts elsewhere say did not happen with him.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
omitted as a body-part term for agency: John <b>13</b>:3</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>harlot 
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>prostitute</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>hate
                </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) In <i>love-hate</i> combinations, we
have said <i>love more than</i> (cp. Genesis <b>29</b>:30 re Rachel and Leah;
Malachi <b>2</b>:1-2 &lt; Romans<b> 9</b>:3 re Jacob and Esau). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Sometimes we
have taken <i>hate</i> to mean <i>Loves less than</i> (Luke <b>18</b>:46). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>Disregard</i>
or <i>neglect</i> can work occasionally (as in Ephesians <b>5</b>:29). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>NOTE: This kind of
weakening, strengthening, and bending of terms comes from the Hebrew tendency
to use words for what is a less degree of the same thing, what leads to the
same thing, what grows out of the same thing, what is like the same thing.
Jesus demonstrates the principle in the Sermon on the Mount when he “enlarges”
the murder prohibition to include hate, and the adultery prohibition to include
fostering lust (Matthew <b>5</b>:21-27; cp. 1 John <b>3</b>:15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>he                    </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
always <i>he/himself </i>in reference to the Holy Spirit because the Spirit as
to nature has personal characteristics. The mistake in <i>King James Version</i>
at Romans<b> 8</b>:26 was perhaps a slip because of the grammatically neuter
Greek word for spirit/Spirit (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πνεῦμα</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
Grammatical gender does not correspond to physical sex reference particularly.
Note the same issue applies to </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>βρέφος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(n.) “baby.” The <i>American Standard Version</i> likewise makes a doubtful use
of <i>ít</i> for the Spirit in Acts<b> 8</b>:16: <i>“as yet <u>it</u> had
fallen on none of them”</i> (changed to <i>he</i> in <i>NASB</i>). The <i>ASV</i>
does similarly in 1 Peter<b> 1</b>:11. <i>   </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>It</i> is
the translation for all the several other uses of </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πνεῦμα</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
that do not refer to deity: spirit <i>vs</i>.<i> letter</i>, spirit as <i>part
of the human make-up</i>; <i>attitude</i>, <i>wind</i>, <i>breath</i>. The <i>it</i>
pronoun we have used as well for <i>demons</i> with their depersonalizing
effects on the ones they possessed; we have applied <i>he</i> to God and angels</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>head
               </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) <i>head</i> when referring to a
person’s physical head (1 Corinthians <b>11</b>:1-10, <i>etc.</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>head</i>
when referring to Christ as “head” of the church (Ephesians <b>1</b>:22;
Colossians <b>1</b>:18, <i>etc.</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<i>head</i> as the one responsible for the family, including his wife
(Ephesians<b> 5</b>:23)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>hear</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     used
only for hearing a sound , not for listening or obeying (<i>heeding</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>heart    </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>mind</i> in Mark<b> 8</b>:17, with <i>to herself</i> in Revelation<b>
18</b>:4</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>heaven</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>οὐρανός</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οὐρανοί</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>unless
translated sky, always rendered <i>heaven</i> in the singular on the
supposition that the Greek plural reflects the Hebrew word, which is a dual
form.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) <i>heaven</i> for God’s dwelling
place (note Paul’s <i>third heaven</i> and <i>Paradise</i>; 2 Corinthians <b>12</b>:2)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
sky</i> for where birds fly, clouds drift, and celestial bodies appear. <i>Heaven
and earth</i> changed to <i>earth and sky</i> in the combination: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>5</b>:18; <b>24</b>:35; Mark<b> 13</b>:31; Luke <b>10</b>:21; <b>16</b>:17; <b>21</b>:33;
Acts <b>17</b>:24; 2 Peter <b>3</b>:7, 13; Revelation<b> 20</b>:11; <b>21</b>:1<sup>2
</sup></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                              
The uncertainty between option (a) and (b) can be difficult to overcome. In
Colossians <b>1</b>:16 and 20, for example, do not seem to use <i>heaven </i>the
same way though they are near each other, It seems surprising to say that
Christ <i>“created everything in heaven(s)”</i> (<b>1</b>:16) if it means God’s
dwelling place; but in the second text it seems surprising to speak of Christ’s<i>
“making peace with things in the sky”</i> (<b>1</b>:20). So <i>CV </i>has <i>sky</i>
in the first (with Christ as firstborn over all creation, which he could pre-exist)
and<i> heaven </i>in the second. Perhaps <i>heaven</i> refers to everything
that is not earth, whether sky or Paul’s “third heaven” (2 Corinthians <b>12</b>:2);
so the referents are not distinguishable terminologically but by context—with
the possibility of blurred usage. Creation predominates here in the first verse
while reconciliation predominates in the second.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
capitalized when a substitute for <i>God</i>: Luke <b>10</b>:18, 21</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Hebrew</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
        (a) The <i>Hebr</i>- root is once translated “Aramaic” in John <b>19</b>:20
(cp. Luke <b>23</b>:38<sup>ms</sup>), one of the three languages of the
superscription on the cross. Presumably Pilate would not have known classical
“Hebrew.” </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The next entry (b)
would justify saying “Hebrew” even here for a different reason, and the short
inscription would probably not have involved a Hebrew-Aramaic variant since
Pilate probably wrote in a consonantal text (vowel points came centuries later).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)
translated <i>Hebrew </i>elsewhere<i> </i>in John’s writings because the
translation of “Hebrew” names into Greek equivalents implies consideration for
the Greek audience he primarily addressed: John <b>5</b>:2; <b>19</b>:13, 17;
Revelation <b>9</b>:11; <b>16</b>:16. A Gentile readership might not operate
with a Hebrew-Aramaic distinction in mind. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
Acts <b>26</b>:14 carries <i>Hebrew</i> on the chance that the Lord in his
appearance may have addressed Paul in classical Hebrew, which might explain how
the fellow travelers heard a voice (Acts <b>26</b>:14) but did not understand
(Acts <b>22</b>:9) Christ. <i>Hebrew</i> also appears in Paul’s defense before the
mob in Jerusalem, who gave him their attention when they heard him speak in <i>Hebrew
</i>(Acts <b>21</b>:40; <b>22</b>:2). Was it because they heard him speaking in
Aramaic rather than Greek, or because he was speaking in classical Hebrew
rather than Aramaic? Did their <u>greater</u> silence (<b>22</b>:2) come from
having to concentrate more intensely to understand his Hebrew? All these
notations depend on how well the general populace would understand classical
Hebrew. Nehemiah <b>8</b>:1-8 speaks of translating the Law so the people could
understand. Those new repatriates to Palestine evidently did not have a good grasp
of the Hebrew in the Torah.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(e)
translated <i>Hebrews</i> when in reference to nationality/race (Acts <b>6</b>:1;
2 Corinthians <b>11</b>:22; Philippians <b>3</b>:3<sup>2</sup>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        As
it works out, <i>Hebrew</i> could probably have been sufficient in all these
cases: because the same word customarily covered both for foreign audiences,
because Pilate’s consonantal heading would have been the same in Hebrew or
Aramaic, or because circumstances of usage in Paul’s conversion and the report
of it to the Jerusalem mob are not clear enough to warrant inferring classical
Hebrew. Such are the uncertainties of translation work.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>henceforth
  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>from now on</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>herein
  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>he’s                 </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
contraction for <i>he is</i> in most cases; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) in quite a
number of passages, a contraction for <i>he has</i>: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>11</b>:18; <b>17</b>:12; Mark <b>7</b>:37; Luke <b>4</b>:18;<b> 7</b>:23; <b>14</b>:29;
John<b> 4</b>:22, 24, 26, 27; <b>6</b>:39, 46; <b>10</b>:20; <b>11</b>:25, 39; <b>15</b>:16;
<b>16</b>:13; Acts <b>13</b>:33; <b>17</b>:31<sup>2</sup>; <b>21</b>:28; Romans
<b>1</b>:20; <b>2</b>:6; <b>5</b>:11; 2 Corinthians <b>1</b>:19; Philippians<b>
3</b>:26<sup>2</sup>; Colossians <b>1</b>:8; 2 Timothy <b>1</b>:11. 14; 1 Peter
<b>2</b>:21; <b>3</b>:22; 2 Peter <b>1</b>:9; 1 John <b>4</b>:13, 20<sup>2</sup>;
Revelation <b>22</b>:12.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>holy     </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Its
basic<i> </i>meaning is <i>set apart from general use to a special one</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i> </i>That
has led to using <i>holy</i> for deity, angels, and divine things.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) legitimate as
opposed to illegitimate children: 1 Corinthians<b> 7</b>:14 in reference to the
offspring of a mixed marriage with an unbeliever; possibly also Luke <b>1</b>:35
regarding the <i>Holy One</i> [</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>βρέφος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
neuter] <i>begotten</i> as in <i>“the</i> [considered] <i>legitimate [baby]
will be called the Son of the Most High”</i> (<i>vs.</i> being the bastard son
of an unmarried couple)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(pay)
homage</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> or <i>bowed down to</i> (a) when directed to other
than God: Acts <b>10</b>:25, Cornelius to Peter (+cp. Matthew <b>2</b>:2, 8,
11)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>worship</i> when directed to deity</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            Keeping
the ideal distinction proves uncertain in the New Testament historical books
because of the difficulty of assessing the awareness of, say, the <u>Magi</u>
when they see Jesus (Matthew <b>2</b>:11), the <u>disciples</u> in the early
parts of the Lord’s ministry, <u>members of the general population</u> that
come to Jesus for help and healing. The same problem corresponds with whether
to capitalize “lord” in reference to deity.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>hour                </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>hour</i> used only for a specific amount of time: <i>“third hour of the
day,”</i> <i>etc.</i>, 9 o’clock</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
replaced with <i>time</i> for an indefinite point in time </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) not for a <i>minute</i>
(Galatians <b>2</b>:5) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d) <i>a.m.</i>
and <i>p.m.</i> could replace <i>o’clock</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>house/household  
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sometimes
replaced with <i>family</i>, which can allow for extended family and perhaps
servants: John<b> 4</b>:53; 1 Timothy <b>3</b>:12<i>   </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>household</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> appears
when a much larger situation is indicated: <i>Caesar’s household </i>(Philippians
<b>4</b>:22); likewise in Mark <b>14</b>:35; Acts <b>7</b>:10 (Pharaoh); Acts <b>10</b>:1,
7, 14 (Cornelius); 2 Timothy<b> 2</b>:21.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>however</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
Between adversative statements, replaced by <i>but</i> except in Philippians <b>3</b>:16
and Hebrews<b> 2</b>:9. <i>However </i>as an adverb of manner occurs in Matthew
<b>17</b>:12 = Mark <b>9</b>:13; 2 Corinthians <b>1</b>:20.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>husbandman</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
<i>vine dresser </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>if          </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaces
the more formal <i>whether</i> for introducing indirect questions. English
speakers seldom distinguish between <i>if</i> for condition and <i>whether</i>
for indirect question (</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew <b>26</b>:63;
Mark <b>3</b>:2; <b>10</b>:2; <b>11</b>:13; <b>15</b>:36, 44: Luke <b>3</b>:1, 15;
<b>6</b>:7; <b>14</b>:28; <b>14</b>:1;<b> 23</b>:6; John <b>7</b>:17<sup>2</sup>;
<b>9</b>:18, 25; Acts<b> 4</b>:19; <b>10</b>:18; <b>17</b>:11; <b>19</b>:2; 1
Corinthians <b>1</b>:16; 2 Corinthians <b>2</b>:9; <b>13</b>:5). Interestingly,
the Greek word </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εἰ</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>regularly
serves both purposes as well. <i>Whether </i>has been kept for statements of
alternatives between real options; <i>if</i> addresses positive <i>vs.</i>
negative (conditionality). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>immediately</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
We have greatly reduced the number of usages, especially in Mark’s gospel (for </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εὐθύς</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
Mark seems to use it like </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οὖν</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(<i>then</i>) in John’s gospel, and not much more specific than <i>and</i> (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>καί</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>and
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>δέ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
in the other gospels. Such frequent usage “wears the edge off” of <i>immediately</i>
and reduces it to something like <i>then</i> or <i>next</i> in what the writer wants
to tell</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in/inside/within</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
In Luke’s classic quotation of the Lord (<b>17</b>:21), we have departed
typical renderings (<i>inside you, within you, in you, in your midst</i>) in
favor of <i>interpersonal</i>. </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Ἐντός</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>occurs
only twice in the New Testament—here and in Matthew <b>23</b>:26. Knowing what
the “kingdom” turned out to be, we have read back into Jesus’ wording the
character of the “kingdom” as we understand it. It has a non-locational nature<i>—“not
here or there”</i>; it is held together by the <i>“bonds of love</i>,<i>”</i>
not by geography, nationality, race, or some other non-interpersonal characteristic;
it is not spread or established by military activity (John <b>18</b>:36) but by
influence (Matthew <b>28</b>:18-20), and it is eternal and timeless (2 Peter<b>
1</b>:11).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in
order that + clause</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    replaced by an infinitive phrase to
indicate purpose whenever possible: “I’m saying this <i>to benefit</i> you” (1
Corinthians <b>7</b>:35)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>iniquity    
sin</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>insurrectionist</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
the translation used for Barabbas and the two “thieves” crucified with Jesus. <i>Rebel</i>
seems not strong enough because it does not necessarily indicate their being
part of a larger group (Mark <b>15</b>:7). Their designation </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>λῃστής</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>can
be thief, but in this circumstance something more serious must be involved than
stealing. Murder was involved for Barabbas in their endeavors (Mark <b>15</b>:7;
Luke <b>23</b>:19, 25; Acts <b>3</b>:14). An insurrectionist is someone
