involved in trying to overthrow the government or to incite riot. In that
endeavor, murder fits and would be a more likely crime for carrying the death
penalty, especially with the Roman government.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>into</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      (a)
usually replaced by <i>to</i> for destination as to a city or province</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
</i>sometimes replaced by <i>in</i> when speaking of entering something: <i>“He
got <u>in</u> the boat.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>is      
  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>rendered<i>
amounts to</i>: Romans<b> 2</b>:25; 1 Corinthians <b>3</b>:19; Ephesians <b>5</b>:5,
28; Colossians <b>3</b>:5; James<b> 4</b>:4; 1 John <b>2</b>:15</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify;line-height:
normal'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>             <i>is
characterized by</i> (1 John <b>4</b>:16)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>it          </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
references impersonal things or abstractions </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
</i>generally<i> </i>avoided as an expletive as in “<i>It</i> is necessary to
fulfill all righteousness.”</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (c)
used instead of <i>her</i> for a country, ship, city, <i>etc.</i>, as
traditional references</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in;line-height:normal'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d)<i> </i>used
also for demons except in Matthew <b>12</b>:44-45</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in;line-height:normal'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(e) not used for
the Holy Spirit (in contrast to ASV for Acts <b>8</b>:16; ASV for Romans <b>5</b>:5;
Ephesians<b> 1</b>:13-14 (<i>which</i>); KJV for Romans<b> 8</b>:21)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-40.5pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Jehovah</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
not used; <i>Jehovah </i>is an artificial word created from mixing the
consonants of the Hebrew Tetragrammaton (</span><span lang=HE dir=RTL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>יהוה</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span>), God’s personal name, and the vowels from</span><span dir=RTL></span><span
lang=HE dir=RTL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=RTL></span> אֲדֹנָי<b> </b></span><span dir=LTR></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span>(<i>“my Lord”</i>). The result is </span><span lang=HE dir=RTL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>יְהֹוָה</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-40.5pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>joy</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         used
often, even though the word does not commonly appear in conversational English.
In some places we have replaced it with <i>excitement</i> and <i>excited</i>:
Matthew <b>13</b>:44; <b>28</b>:8; Mark <b>16</b>:8; Luke <b>10</b>:17, 20<sup>2</sup>;
John <b>20</b>:20; Acts <b>12</b>:4; <b>15</b>:3. <i>Happy</i> serves also—as
something of a weak equivalent that has the feel of depending on what “happens.”
Joy has more the feel of a sense of well-being or positive mental attitude; but
those ideas are difficult to capture in efficient wording</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>kid</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>       sometimes
used in place of <i>child/children</i> as an affectionate term or as a term for
immature people: <sup>+</sup>Matthew <b>7</b>:11; <b>11</b>:16; <b>15</b>:26; <b>19</b>:13,
14; <b>21</b>:15; Mark <b>7</b>:11, 28; <b>10</b>:13, 14, 15; Luke <b>7</b>:32;
<b>11</b>:7, 13; <b>18</b>:16, 17; 1 Corinthians <b>13</b>:11; <b>14</b>:20;
Ephesians <b>6</b>:4; 1 Thessalonians <b>2</b>:7, 11</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>kill</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>       (a)
<i>put to death</i> in cases of legal execution </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>murder</i> for killing people
illegally </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>kill</i> rather than <i>slay</i>
for animals and people generally </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>King
of kings</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>  For familiarity purposes, <i>CV</i> keeps the
traditional expression, which always combines with <i>Lord of lords</i> even
though the Hebrew idiom has no exact English equivalent. The closest might be
something like, <i>“He’s a man among men,”</i> or <i>“the best of the best.”</i>
It is a kind of superlative, meaning <i>“the Lord/King over everything else,”</i>
<i>“the lord/king with the highest ranking among lords/kings.”</i> See 1 Timothy
<b>6</b>:15; Revelation <b>17</b>:14; <b>19</b>:16. In earlier political
situations like the king of Babylon, Nebuchadnezzar was the king over the kings
of individual subdued countries. That arrangement may also contribute to the
idiom.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>kingdom
of God   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) <i>kingdom of God</i> if it sounds more like a
title</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
<i>God’s kingdom</i> if it sounds like a description—note parallelism in the
“needle’s eye” texts: <sup>+</sup>Matthew <b>19</b>:24; Mark <b>10</b>:23, 25;
Luke <b>18</b>:25 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>lampstand</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
<i>lampstand</i> in </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Hebrews <b>9</b>:2;
Revelation <b>1</b>:12, 20; <b>2</b>:1, 5; <b>11</b>:4</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
simply<i> stand</i>: Matthew <b>5</b>:15; Mark <b>4</b>:21; Luke <b>8</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>law                  </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
</i>Even when articular, </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>νόμος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>translates
to <i>law</i> (<u>identity</u>, lower case) when contrasted to grace/faith: <i>“Moses
gave law; Messiah brought grace and truth [reality]”</i> (John<b> 1</b>:17);
law as <u>a kind of thing</u>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
</i>translated <i>the Law</i> as an <u>identity</u>—not in contrast to
faith-grace—but as if in contrast to another law. Galatians<b> 3</b>:15-26 is a
text where we have mixed <i>law</i> (kind of thing) and <i>the Law</i> (the
Mosaic Law as an identity). The Mosaic Law, of course, has the characteristics
of law as such. In Paul’s comments, <i>the Law</i> is <i>CV</i>’s rendering in<b>
3</b>:17, 19 and <i>law</i> in <b>3</b>:18, 21, 23 because Paul is concerned
with the<u> kind of thing</u> law is in contrast to grace/faith/promise/give.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<i>CV</i> translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>νόμος</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> with quotes
around “<i>law</i>” (of Christ) to show a specialized use of the word to refer
to the gospel in Christianity as the corresponding element for the Law of Moses
in Judaism—even though the gospel in the Christian system is different in kind
from the Law in the Mosaic system. Christ’s system (“law”) is correlative with
the Law of Moses, so Paul applies the same term to it “adjusted.” As such, it
refers to a pattern of things: Romans <b>3</b>:27<sup>3</sup>; Galatians <b>6</b>:2;
1 Corinthians<b> 9</b>:21. A similar “principle” usage—but aside from the
Mosaic law—appears in Romans <b>7</b>:21, 23<sup>2</sup>; 25.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
law when referring to <u>a</u> law within the full body of law</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>leaven</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  replaced
with <i>yeast </i>wherever possible (except for 1 Corinthians <b>5</b>:8 and
references to the standardized title Feast of Unleavened Bread)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>lest</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      replaced
with <i>for fear that</i>, <i>so that . . . not</i> as introductions to fear
clauses; general circumlocution may also replace the fear clause: <i>“lest at
any time you trip over a rock”</i> becomes <i>“so you’ll never trip over a
rock”</i> (Matthew <b>4</b>:6)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>let</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                    (a)
avoided wherever possible as a translation for the Greek third person
imperative: <i>“let him hear.”</i> Strictly speaking, English has no third
person imperative; English substitutes the <i>let</i> construction, in which <i>let</i>
loses its sense of <i>“allow”</i> and approaches an imperatival value.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
Let’s</i> for hortatory subjunctive (first person plural), that is,
exhortation: <i>“He’s the heir; let’s kill him”</i> (Luke <b>20</b>:14; often
elsewhere).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>like</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                  (a)
frequently a conjunction in place of <i>as</i>: <i>“Shouldn’t you have been
merciful like I was with you?”</i> (Matthew <b>18</b>:33; see also <b>5</b>:48;
<b>6</b>:2, 7, 10, 12; <b>13</b>:35, 44; <b>18</b>:33; <b>20</b>:28; <b>25</b>:32;
<b>27</b>:10; <b>28</b>:6; <i>etc.</i> cp. 1 Corinthians <b>16</b>:10).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
retained as a preposition: <i>“like a mustard seed” </i>(Matthew<b> 13</b>:31, <i>etc.</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>lo</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         usually
omitted along with <i>behold</i> as translations of </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἰδού</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ἴδε</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>. English often dispenses with
“attention fixers,” perhaps instead using “look” (I want to help you, but . . .
”). Note <i>Look</i> in John <b>19</b>:5, 14.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>L</span></i><i><span
style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><span
style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (a)
all caps when obviously referring to the deity Yahveh: L</span><span
style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                  </span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>angel
of the L</span></i><i><span style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Matthew
<b>1</b>:20, 24 [omitted]; <b>2</b>:13, 19; <b>28</b>:2; Luke <b>1</b>:11; <b>2</b>:9b;
Acts <b>5</b>:19; <b>8</b>:26; <b>12</b>:7, 23)  </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Old
Testament quotations: Matthew <b>5</b>:23; <b>21</b>:9; <b>27</b>:10; Mark <b>12</b>:11;
Luke <b>4</b>:18; Acts <b>2</b>:20, 21; <b>4</b>:26; <b>7</b>:33, 49; Hebrews <b>7</b>:21;
<b>12</b>:6; 1 Peter <b>1</b>:25; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
kept in lower case (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>) for people
addressing other people and angels or when someone speaking to Jesus was not
likely to have recognized him as deity </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<i>sir</i> in several cases to Jesus: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew<b>
8</b>:2, 6, 8, 21; <b>9</b>:28 (omitted); <b>17</b>:15; Luke <b>5</b>:12; <b>7</b>:6;
<b>9</b>:59; <b>19</b>:8; John<b> 4</b>:11, 15, 19, 49; <b>5</b>:7; <b>6</b>:34;
[[<b>8</b>:11]].</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        In
something of a special case, we have used <i>Sir</i> as Saul’s address to the
Lord during his appearance to him (Acts <b>9</b>:5; <b>22</b>:8; <b>26</b>:15).
The translation assumption was that Saul at first did not know who he was
talking to—an angel, the angel of the L</span><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
a person Saul had previously put to death, the “angel” of an executed disciple.
Otherwise, why ask? That should have been clear from the preceding question <i>“Why
are you persecuting me?”</i> Maybe it was more of a bewildered response with no
definite addressee in mind. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<i>sir</i> to others besides Jesus: </span><b><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>25</b>:11; <b>27</b>:63; Luke<b> 2</b>:9a; <b>13</b>:8, 25; <b>19</b>:25;
John <b>20</b>:15; <b>12</b>:21; Acts <b>9</b>:5 (cp. <b>22</b>:10); <b>10</b>:4
(Cornelius to the angel), 14; <b>11</b>:8; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:6 (Sarah to
Abraham); John to one of the twenty-four elders in Revelation <b>7</b>:14</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            Tying
capitalization to deity creates the same problem that shows up with <i>“worship”
vs</i>. <i>“pay homage, bow down to.” </i>See below under <i>worship</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Lord
of lords </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>Because of its familiarity, <i>CV</i> keeps the
traditional expression that is always coupled with “King of kings” even though
the Hebrew idiom does not have a close English parallel. “<u>X</u> of <u>x</u>”
is a kind of superlative reference, meaning “<i>the Lord/King over every other
lord/king</i>,<i>” “the one with the highest ranking among lords/kings.”</i>
See </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>1 Timothy <b>6</b>:15;
Revelation <b>17</b>:14; <b>19</b>:16.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>L</span></i><i><span
style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
</i>the all-caps rendering of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
in the New Testament in quotations of, or references to, the Old Testament that
carry the Tetragrammaton or refer to it: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <b>1</b>:22;
<b>2</b>:15; <b>3</b>:3; <b>4</b>:7, 10; <b>5</b>:33; <b>21</b>:9, 42; <b>22</b>:37,
44; <b>23</b>:39; <b>27</b>:10; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Mark</span></b><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
1</span></b><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:3;<b>
12</b>:29<sup>2</sup>, 30, 36; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <b>2</b>:23;
<b>3</b>:4; <b>4</b>:8, 12, 18; <b>4</b>:19;<b> 10</b>:27; <b>13</b>:35; <b>19</b>:38;
<b>20</b>:37, 42; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <b>1</b>:23;
<b>12</b>:13, 38<sup>2</sup>; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

21, 25, 35, 39; <b>3</b>:22; <b>4</b>:26; <b>7</b>:31, 33, 49; <b>8</b>:39; <b>13</b>:47;
<b>15</b>:17<sup>2</sup>; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) the rendering
of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in the New Testament in references
to other than the Lord Jesus and having the phraseology of Old Testament texts
that refer to the God of Israel: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew</span></b><span

<b>2</b>:13, 19; <b>11</b>:25; <b>24</b>:22; <b>28</b>:2; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

[<b>2</b>:28]; <b>11</b>:10; <b>12</b>:11; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><b><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)
in the expression <i>“angel of the L</i></span><i><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>”</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>1</b>:20; <b>2</b>:13, 19; <b>28</b>:2; Luke <b>1</b>:11; <b>2</b>:9; <b>5</b>:19;
<b>8</b>:26; <b>12</b>:7, 23</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d) in the mouth
of Jesus to God: Matthew </span><b><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>24</span></b><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:22; Mark </span><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>13</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:20;
Luke </span><b><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>10</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:21;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Lord</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    kept
in c &amp; lc when referring to Jesus by the authors of the New Testament books
or as expressed by Jesus’ disciples to him: Matthew <b>8</b>:25; <b>14</b>:28;
1 Timothy <b>1</b>:14, and the majority of New Testament references.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (a)
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
variously translated when not referring to Jesus: Luke <b>10</b>:2 (harvest
foreman); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Acts <b>25</b>:26
(my superior); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>master</i>
of a slave (Matthew <b>6</b>:24; <b>10</b>:24, 25; <b>13</b>:27; <b>18</b>:31; <b>24</b>:48;
<b>25</b>:20, 22, 24; Luke <b>12</b>:36, 37, 42, 46; <b>13</b>:8; <b>14</b>:22;<b>
19</b>:16, 18, 20, 25; John <b>13</b>:16; <b>15</b>:15; Acts <b>16</b>:16, 19,
30 (<i>sirs</i>); Romans<b> 14</b>:4; Ephesians <b>6</b>:5, 9; Colossians <b>3</b>:22;
<b>4</b>:1;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<i>sir</i> by general audience member to Jesus and others: Matthew <b>8</b>:2,
6, 8, 21, 25; <b>9</b>:28; <b>14</b>:28, 30; <b>15:</b>22, 25, 27; <b>16</b>:22;
<b>25</b>:11, 22; Mark <b>7</b>:28; Luke<b> 14</b>:23; John <b>4</b>:11, 15,
19, 49; <b>5</b>:7; <b>6</b>:34, 68; <b>12</b>:21; <b>20</b>:15; Acts <b>16</b>:30
(<i>sirs</i>); Revelation <b>7</b>:14.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (e)
<i>“Lord of the Sabbath”</i> handled differently from literal wording: Matthew <b>12</b>:8
= Mark <b>2</b>:28 = Luke <b>6</b>:5 </span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(<i>“</i></span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Person
takes precedence over Sabbath.”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (f)
<i>owner</i> in Matthew <b>20</b>:8; <b>21</b>:40; Mark<b> 12</b>:9; <b>13</b>:35;
Luke <b>19</b>:33; <b>20</b>:13, 15; Acts <b>16</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (g)
omitted where the number of vocatives seems excessive as per English custom:
Matthew <b>15</b>:27;<b> 16</b>:22;<b> 20</b>:33; Mark <b>10</b>:20; Luke <b>9</b>:54;
<b>10</b>:16; <b>11</b>:1; <b>17</b>:37; <b>19</b>:8, 18; John<b> 13</b>:37; <b>17</b>:24;
Acts <b>6</b>:3; <b>13</b>:38; <b>26</b>:7</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>loud
voice</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>    <i>shout</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>love     </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
in a few cases by <i>care/caring</i> to get away from the romantic—or at least
emotional—connotation the English term has picked up: John <b>12</b>:43; 2
Corinthians<b> 2</b>:4, 8; James <b>1</b>:12; <b>2</b>:5; 1 John <b>3</b>:10,
11; Revelation <b>3</b>:19 (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>φιλέω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>lust/s</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    replaced
by <i>desires</i> or <i>drives</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>man                 </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
retained when referring to a husband (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀνήρ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
and when in direct contrast to woman. When in contrast to God, animal, child,
or idea, some kind of appropriate alternative comes into play for inclusive
language purposes; see next comments.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
replaced by <i>a person</i>, <i>people</i>, indefinite pronouns (2 Corinthians <b>4</b>:6;
Revelation <b>18</b>:23), <i>you </i>advisedly (John <b>11</b>:9-11),<i> they</i>
advisedly (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄνθρωπος</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>), <i>(hu)mankind</i>
(John <b>1</b>:4; Acts <b>15</b>:17; <b>22</b>:15; Revelation <b>9</b>:15, 18,
20), <i>fellow(s)</i> (Acts <b>16</b>:20, <i>etc.</i>), <i>servants</i> (3 John
8).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
replaced by plurals: 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:23-25, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<i>Christians</i> (Galatians <b>1</b>:2)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>many               </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
usually omitted as overused compared to English custom; left out or replaced
especially if used as a pronoun/substantive adjective</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) often replaced
with <i>a lot of</i>/<i>lots of</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>marry</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  replacement
for the habitual phraseology <i>marry and given in marriage</i>. In light of
the arranged marriage custom, Greek/Hebrew idiom mentions both sides of the
process. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>master</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>             (a)
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>δεσπότης</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>; <i>Lord/lord</i>
usually renders </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐπιστάτα</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, a vocative term
for the Lord unique to Luke: </span><b><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup></b><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>5</span></b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:5;
<b>8</b>:24, 43; <b>9</b>:33, 49; <b>17</b>:12</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>may</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     for
contingent action only: <i>“That may happen in two weeks”</i>; hence, used for <i>“may”</i>
<i>vs</i>. <i>“is/will</i>,<i>” rather than “may”</i> <i>vs. “can.” </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(the)
morrow</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>     <i>tomorrow</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(“in/into the) <i>name</i>
(of”) (a) shortens to (<i>in/into</i>)<i> . . . <u>x</u></i>. The customary
phraseology seems unnecessarily long in some “name” usages. <i>Believe in the
name of</i> shortens to <i>believe in</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>Name</i>
draws attention to “identity with”; so we have not removed the longer form in
the Great Commission (Matthew <b>28</b>:18-20): Jesus charged the apostles with
presenting the good news to people in every nation and identifying them with
the Messiah. The same emphasis on identity comes with a longer wording of the
first command to identify with Jesus as the Messiah, so that on the basis of
that identity with him—total, permanent, exclusive—God would view them as
sinless like Messiah, grant his Spirit to them, and incorporate them into the
body of Christ (Acts<b> 2</b>:38-42). The baptizing in those texts was what the
people were commanded to do as the manner of expressing their willingness to
respond to God’s condition for his gifts (cp. Galatians<b> 6</b>:3, 27). A
parallel example surfaces in Paul’s comment to the Corinthians: he was glad he had
not baptize more people than he did, lest the critics in Corinth would claim he
baptized into his own name (1 Corinthians<b> 1</b>:15). Cp. comments above on <i>for
the forgiveness of sins</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>             </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>nation</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>              (a)
usually becomes <i>country</i> in cases of national reference</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
avoided as a designation for a smaller people group like the Kickapoo nation;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            replaced
by <i>Gentiles</i> when in contrast to Israel: Matthew <b>12</b>:18, 21 (&lt;
Isaiah <b>42</b>:1, 4); <b>24</b>:9, 14)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(fell
on his) neck</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    <i>hugged</i> (Luke <b>15</b>:20; Acts<b>
20</b>:37)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>nobody</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
replaces <i>no one</i>; indefinite pronouns in <i>___body</i> take precedence
over <i>____one</i>: <i>anybody</i>, <i>everybody</i>, <i>nobody</i>, <i>somebody</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>none</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
can be treated as singular or plural. In Romans<b> 14</b>:7, for example, <i>CV</i>
uses it as plural to conform to inclusive language: <i>“None of us live to
ourselves or die to ourselves,”</i> instead of <i>“None of us lives to himself
. . .”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>no
one</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    
<i>nobody</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>nor</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      dropped
even when it would combine with <i>neither</i>; replaced by <i>or</i> </span><span
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John
<b>9</b>:3; Acts <b>15</b>:10; <b>19</b>:37; Galatians<b> 5</b>:6; <b>6</b>:15</span><span
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                   (a)
negatives in modern usage appear before the verb rather than the direct object:
<i>“We don’t have such a custom”</i> in place of <i>“We have no such custom”</i>
(1 Corinthians <b>11</b>:16);<i> “Love not the world”</i> becomes <i>“Don’t
love the world”</i> (1 John <b>2</b>:15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) double
negatives are not used (including <i>“can’t help but”</i>). They are quite
common in Greek for emphasis—even triple negatives (Matthew <b>25</b>:9, </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μήποτε</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οὐ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μὴ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>“There will <u>certainly</u> <u>not</u> <u>at all</u> be enough for you and
us”</i>)!</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) negatives as
part of litotes fall away because we have eliminated most examples of it.
Litotes is a figure of speech that affirms by denying the opposite. The effect
is emphasis or variety of expression; <i>“No mean city”</i> becomes <i>“a
prominent city”</i> (Acts <b>21</b>:39). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>O</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         always
omitted before vocatives as per current English custom: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>15</b>:28; <b>17</b>:17; Mark <b>9</b>:19; Luke <b>9</b>:41; <b>24</b>:25;
Acts <b>1</b>:1; <b>13</b>:10; <b>18</b>:14; <b>27</b>:21; Romans<b> 2</b>:1,
3; <b>9</b>:20; <b>11</b>:33; Galatians <b>3</b>:1; 1 Timothy <b>6</b>:11, 20;
James <b>2</b>:20</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>of</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         <i>CV
</i>reduces the number of <i><u>of</u></i><u>’s</u> as much as possible because
they can be too ambiguous. <i>Of</i> is the standard equivalent for the Greek
genitive case when it ties one noun to another or indicates that part of the
object is affected by the verb. We have supplied other, more specific
prepositions to satisfy English expectancy as per context and nature of the
case.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
of</i> for appositional genitive is sometimes omitted: <i>“the cities of Sodom
and Gomorrah”</i> becomes <i>“Sodom and Gomorrah”</i> or <i>“the cities Sodom
and Gomorrah” </i>(Acts <b>10</b>:22; John <b>3</b>:22). When readers can
likely tell that the preposition’s object is a city rather than a country, <i>etc.</i>,
<i>cities of</i> is unnecessary.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
replaced with <i>about</i> as in <i>“the gospel of Christ”</i> changed to <i>“the
good news about Christ”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
replaced with <i>’s</i>: We have usually kept <i>kingdom of God</i> to make
noticeable the difference between Matthew’s <i>kingdom of heaven </i>(except <s>6:33</s>;
<b>12</b>:28; <b>19</b>:24; <b>21</b>:31,<s> 43</s>) in place of <i>kingdom of
God </i>in parallels in the other synoptic gospels. <i>Church of God</i> keeps
the <i>of</i> construction (except Acts <b>20</b>:28) in parallel to <i>kingdom
of God/heaven.</i> See essay entitled <i>“Kingdom of Heaven/Kingdom of
God/Church.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(d) replaced with an adjective for
the second noun in descriptive genitive usages: <i>“God of peace”</i> becomes <i>“peace-giving
God”</i>;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“money
of blood”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes <i>“blood money” </i>(Matthew<b> 27</b>:6);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“judge
of unrighteousness”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes <i>“unrighteous judge”</i> (Luke<b>
18</b>:6);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“unity
of the spirit”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes <i>“spiritual unity”</i> (Ephesians
<b>4</b>:3)<i>;</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“scheming
of deceit”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes <i>“deceitful scheming”</i> (Ephesians<b> 4</b>:14);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“sons
of disobedience” becomes  disobedient people” </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Ephesians<b>
5</b>:6); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“the
sword of the Spirit” </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>becomes <i>“a spiritual sword” </i>(Ephesians
<b>6</b>:17);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        <i>“evil
heart of disbelief”</i> becomes <i>“an evil, disbelieving heart”</i> (Hebrews <b>3</b>:12);
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> “a
hearer of forgetfulness”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> become <i>“a forgetful hearer”</i>
(James <b>1</b>:25);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <i>“</i>children
of obedience” becomes <i>“obedient children”</i> (1 Peter <b>1</b>:14).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Note also Matthew <b>5</b>:22;
Galatians <b>5</b>:22.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>On the ambiguity of the genitive, see
above under <i>“Ambiguities in the Greek Language Itself.”</i> The same
ambiguity pertains to the Hebrew construct state in the Old Testament and the
“of” prepositional phrases in English. The proliferation of genitive
constructions in the New Testament comes in part from the fact that New
Testament writers were operating from a Hebrew-Aramaic background.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-31.5pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>once</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
 <i>CV </i>has translated<i> </i></span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἅπαξ</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(once)
once and for all </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>to keep it as a time word distinguishable
from number, from <i>one time vs. two</i>: Romans <b>6</b>:10; Hebrews <b>7</b>:29;
<b>9</b>:12. 26; <b>10</b>:2; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:18; Jude 3. 5.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>or                    </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i>
</i>appositional <i>or</i> drops out altogether: Mark <b>4</b>:30, <i>“What can
we compare God’s kingdom to? What’s it like?”</i> <i>vs</i>. <i>“What will we
compare God’s kingdom to, or what’s it like.?”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i> </i>appositional
genitive means the second noun is another way of referring to the same referent
as the first noun, not to a second thing. “<i>City of</i> __” affords an
example: <i>city of Samaria, city of Thyatira, city of Lysea</i>. These phrases
could be reduced to <i>Samaria, Thyatira, Lysea</i> if <i>city of</i> were not
advisable to inform readers that these nouns were cities rather than, say,
provinces.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>one</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      The
indefinite pronoun is not used as a free-standing indefinite pronoun as in <i>“One
does not . . . .”</i> It is used as an indefinite pronoun if modified by a
relative clause as in, <i>“He is the one that did so and so.”</i> It does get
regularly compounded with <i>any-</i>,<i> some-</i>,<i> </i>and <i>every-. </i>In
reference to deity, <i>one</i> is capitalized as an exception to not
capitalizing pronouns in reference to deity.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>one(s)</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <i>The
one(s)</i> ___<i>ing</i> can cover for Greek (a) <u>articular substantive
participles</u> and <u>adjectives</u>. In their place we have often used
indefinite relative pronouns (___ever) or something equivalent. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            The
one(s)</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> can also cover (b) <u>stand-alone Greek articles</u>
that serve as quasi-pronouns. <i>CV</i> substitutes the appropriate personal
pronoun (1 Corinthians <b>15</b>:23).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>One
another</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>  (a) In format one, A does toward B what B also does
to A: <i>one another</i> covers cases like </span><i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“love one
another.”</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
In format two, A does toward B what C does to D, </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>etc</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.
Some of those cases are clear under the <i>one another</i> expression, like </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“They
would kill one another”</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (Revelation<b> 6</b>:4). In other
cases like Ephesians <b>5</b>:21, <i>CV</i> uses <i>one to another, each other </i>to
signal that the author intends this second format. The sometimes suggested
“mutual submission” idea misses the point of the household teaching segment in
Ephesians and elsewhere; masters do not submit to servants or parents to
children.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>only</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     have
allowed some “misplaced” <i>only</i>’s as people do in casual conversation:
Mark <b>8</b>:14; John <b>13</b>:10; 1 Timothy <b>5</b>:23</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>open</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                (a)
used for general purposes;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
replaced with <i>unroll</i> (<i>vs</i>. <i>roll up</i>)<i> </i>in Luke<b> 4</b>:17,
20 and Revelation<b> 5</b>:2-5 regarding a writing because the texts evidently
deal with a scroll </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>own</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     The
intensive reflexive pronouns <i>your own</i>, <i>etc.</i> (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἴδιος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
used for any person and number) are often reduced to a possessive adjective: <i>her/his
own husband/wife</i> becomes <i>her/his husband/wife</i>. Ιntensity seems to be
beside the point in such cases: 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:35; Ephesians <b>5</b>:22,
28, 33; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:1).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>parable&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></i><span
style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>Since&nbsp;<i>parable</i>&nbsp;(</span><span
lang=EL style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>παραβολή</span><span
style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>) hardly ever occurs in English usage
outside a New Testament connection with Jesus' teaching,&nbsp;<i>CV</i>&nbsp;has
replaced it with&nbsp;<i>story</i>&nbsp;in cases that have a flow of action:
Matthew&nbsp;<b>13</b>:3, 10, 13, 18, 24, 34, 35, 36, 53;&nbsp;<b>21</b>:33,
45;&nbsp;<b>22</b>:1; Mark&nbsp;<b>4</b>:2, 10, 11, 13, 33, 34;&nbsp;<b>12</b>:1,
12; Luke&nbsp;<b>8</b>:4, 9, 10, 11;&nbsp;<b>12</b>:16, 41;&nbsp;<b>13</b>:6;&nbsp;<b>15</b>:3;&nbsp;<b>18</b>:1,
9;&nbsp;<b>19</b>:11; 20:9, 19.&nbsp;<i>&nbsp;CV</i>&nbsp;uses&nbsp;<i>illustration</i>&nbsp;in
Matthew&nbsp;<b>15</b>:15; Mark&nbsp;<b>3</b>:23;&nbsp;<b>7</b>:17; Luke&nbsp;<b>5</b>:36;&nbsp;<b>6</b>:39
and&nbsp;<i>example&nbsp;</i>in Luke&nbsp;<b>14</b>:7.&nbsp;<i>CV</i>&nbsp;drops
the word altogether in Matthew&nbsp;<b>13</b>:31, 33 and Luke&nbsp;<b>21</b>:29.&nbsp;<i>Illustration</i>&nbsp;renders&nbsp;</span><span
lang=EL style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>παροιμία</span><span
style='color:#3F3F46;background:white'>&nbsp;in John&nbsp;<b>10</b>:6 and&nbsp;<b>16</b>:25.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>peace   
Peace to you</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> becomes simply <i>“Hello”</i></span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Luke <b>24</b>:36; John <b>20</b>:19, 26 (<b>20</b>:21 not restated)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>people</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>             (a)
for indefinite reference in the plural: Matthew <b>5</b>:11, 13</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>indefinite
reference can be the point of <i>men</i> (</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄνθρωποι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>),
<i>somebody </i>(</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>),
the plural Greek article (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οἱ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>//</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>αἱ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τὰ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
as a quasi-pronoun, plural articular substantive adjectives (Matthew <b>12</b>:16),
plural articular substantive particles.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            Cp. <i>person</i>
below</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
<i>People</i> translates </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>λαός</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
and </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ὄχλος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>; <i>crowd</i> is an alternative term
for them. <i>Multitude</i> has fallen out of familiar usage.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>perhaps</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
replaced by <i>maybe </i>as less formal sounding</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>person
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>for
indefinite reference in the singular: as indicated by a free-standing singular
Greek article, by the indefinite pronoun </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τις</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
by </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄνθρωπος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, by a singular
substantive adjective, by a singular substantive participle</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Cp.
<i>people </i>above<i> </i>for the same possibilities with plural indefinite
references</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>please</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>              (a)
for an urgent request in place of the traditional rendering <i>I beg of you</i>,
for translating </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>δέομαι</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> (</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>8</b>:28; <b>9</b>:39; Acts <b>21</b>:39; <b>26</b>:3; 2 Corinthians <b>5</b>:20)
or </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐρωτάω</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σε</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>14</b>:18, 19).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
simply added to soften the imperative (</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Mark
<b>5</b>:23; Acts <b>9</b>:38; <b>10</b>:26)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>preach</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
usually replaced with <i>present</i> (Acts <b>8</b>:35; <b>14</b>:21; Romans <b>2</b>:16;
<b>15</b>:19, <i>etc.</i>) or <i>deliver </i>(Matthew <b>4</b>:23; <b>9</b>:35;
<b>24</b>:14; Mark <b>1</b>:14; <b>14</b>:9; <b>16</b>:20; Luke <b>3</b>:19, <i>etc.</i>)
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The
English word has become a religious term or one that carries a negative
connotation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>predict</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
one translation of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>προφητεύω</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when
it is, in fact, predicting the future, as a possible rendering of 1 Peter <b>1</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(chief/high)
priests</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> translated <i>chief priests</i> and <i>high priests</i>
depending on whether the text (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀρχιερεύς</span><span
