style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
is speaking only about Annas and Caiaphas or is more generally the main
priests. Matthew <b>26</b>:47 says that chief priests (</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀρχιερέων</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
were at the arrest of Jesus, and the whole group took Jesus to Caiaphas the
high priest (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀρχιερέα</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Hebrews
<b>5-8</b> exegetes Psalm <b>110</b>:4, which says among other things, </span><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“You
are a priest after the order of Melchizedek.”</span></i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> In his comments,
the Hebrew writer switches back and forth between <i>priest</i> and <i>high
priest</i>. </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>CV</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> likewise switches back
and forth as well even though both terms apply to the same person in that text.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-40.5pt'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>prison</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>               (a)
<i>jail</i>, especially if not a lengthy confinement: Matthew <b>5</b>:25; Luke
<b>12</b>:58<sup>2</sup>; <b>20</b>:12; Acts <b>4</b>:3, 19-23; <b>12</b>:4-6,
17; <b>16</b>:23-40; <b>22</b>:4, 19; <b>23</b>:10; 2 Corinthians <b>11</b>:23;
Revelation <b>2</b>:8</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (b)
<i>prison</i> if long term: </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify'><u><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John’s imprisonment</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Matthew <b>11</b>:2; <b>14</b>:3, 10; Mark<b> 6</b>:17, 27; Luke <b>3</b>:20;
John <b>3</b>:24; <b>18</b>:39</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Barabbas</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Matthew <b>27</b>:15, 16; Mark <b>15</b>:6, 7; Luke<b> 23</b>:19, 24</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify'><u><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Paul’s imprisonments</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in
Rome along with his fellow prisoners (Acts <b>23</b>:18; <b>24</b>:27; <b>25</b>:14,
27; <b>27</b>:1, 42; <b>28</b>:17; Romans <b>16</b>:7; Ephesians <b>4</b>:1;
Philippians <b>1</b>:7, 13, 14, 18; Colossians <b>4</b>:3, 10; 2 Timothy<b> 1</b>:8;
<b>2</b>:8, 9; Phil 1, 8, 13, 23 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        <u>the
law</u> as a prison: Romans<b> 7</b>:6. 23</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:
.5in'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            <u>Rome</u>
as a prison: Revelation <b>18</b>:2</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        <u>Spirits
and Satan</u> held in prison: 1 Peter<b> 3</b>:19; 2 Peter <b>2</b>:4;
Revelation<b> 20</b>:7</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        general
reference: Matthew <b>18</b>:30; <b>25</b>:36-44; Luke <b>22</b>:33; Hebrews <b>10</b>:34,
36; <b>13</b>:3<sup>2</sup></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            The
principle about shorter and longer confinement applies to <i>prisoner</i>, <i>imprison</i>,
and <i>imprisonment</i> as well.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>proclaim</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
replaced often with <i>present</i>, <i>announce</i>, or<i> deliver</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>prophecy/prophesy</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <i>Prophesy</i>
can mean (a) <i>predict</i> the future (“foretelling”), which is what usually
comes to mind when people hear the word. That is the way <i>CV</i> translates
it when prediction is apparently the point.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>It
can more broadly (b) <i>speak on behalf of another</i> regardless of content
(“for-telling”). In this use, <i>CV</i> has rendered it <i>communicate</i> in 1
Corinthians <b>14</b>:1-5. Paul contrasts </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>προφητεύω</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>with
<i>“speaking in a language people cannot understand.”</i> Speaking that way
would not be communicating anything; so, actually communicating something must
be the apostle’s meaning for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>προφητεύω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
here. Later, in that same vein, <i>CV</i> says, <i>“If everybody is ‘speaking
on behalf of’ God, and an unbeliever or layman comes in, they’ll be convincing
him and calling him to account”</i> (<b>14</b>:24).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        An
even broader reference (“forth-telling”) happens in Matthew <b>26</b>:68, where
Pilate’s soldiers are slapping the blindfolded Jesus and saying, <i>“Prophesy
to us, Christ; who slapped you?”</i> <i>CV</i> says, (c) <i>“</i>Tell<i> us, ‘Messiah,’
who slapped you?”</i> Here Jesus is not even <i>“speaking for another.”</i> (The
soldiers may have been “hyping” the term as part of their mockery because he
had claimed to be a prophet and the Messiah.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>publican</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    
replaced with <i>tax collector</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>pursue</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
<i>follow</i>, if not with harmful intent (</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>διώκω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>rebel  
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>see
<i>insurrectionist </i>above</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>rebuke
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  replaced
often by the more current word <i>reprimand</i> to avoid the former’s negative
connotation, but kept with Jesus’ commands to the natural elements (Matthew<b>
8</b>:26 = Mark <b>4</b>:19 = Luke <b>8</b>:24) and to demons (Matthew<b> 17</b>:18;
Mark<b> 1</b>:25; Luke <b>9</b>:42) and in Michael’s words to the devil (Jude
9)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>remission</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
<i>forgiveness</i> (of sins)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>reproach</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>         replaced
by <i>disgrace</i>, <i>disparage</i>, and the like      </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>reveal/revelation</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
In texts where these words indicate Christ’s return, <i>CV</i> substitutes <i>coming</i>
or <i>return</i> to clarify the point, even though the two expressions use
different word pictures.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>righteous(ness)
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The
words have disappeared from everyday use, and there are no good substitutes for
them. <i>Good</i> has replaced <i>righteous</i> in several passages even though
it is a weaker term. <i>Goodness</i> works in Luke <b>18</b>:9; John <b>16</b>:10;
Acts <b>13</b>:10; <b>17</b>:31; 2 Corinthians <b>6</b>:14; <b>9</b>:9.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>rule                  </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>manage</i> has been <i>CV</i>’s term in household and church settings: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>1
Timothy <b>3</b>:4, 5; <b>5</b>:14, 17. Also appropriate is <i>be responsible
for</i>, <i>oversee the operation of</i>, <i>have greater authority than</i>.
Words traditionally translated <i>rule</i> cover a greater range of degrees
than the English <i>rule</i>; <i>rule</i> has a “heavy-handed” feel (cp. <i>fear,
hate</i>). Given the fundamental character of the Christian faith as
interpersonal, such a sentiment does not fit Christian leadership in principle.
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        Greek
words traditionally translated <i>rule</i> include </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄρχω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(Mark <b>10</b>:42), </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἡγέομαι</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(Hebrews
<b>13</b>:7, 17, 24 for elders), </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ποιμαίνω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(Matthew <b>2</b>:6, Messiah), </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>προΐστημι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(Romans <b>12</b>:8; 1 Timothy <b>3</b>:4, 5, 12; <b>5</b>:17).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        <i>Rule</i>
and <i>submit</i> are correlative terms (cp. <i>son</i>/<i>father</i>, <i>prophesy</i>/<i>fulfill</i>).
What nuances belong to one belong to the other. What <i>CV</i> has done with
one side, it has endeavored to do with the other. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>Rule/ruler</i> comes in often, as in Titus<b> 3</b>:1; Revelation <b>12</b>:5,
<i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Sabbath 
         </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) capitalized when a reference to Saturday, the
Jewish national “rest day.”</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>the Sabbath</i> for a specific Sabbath: Matthew <b>28</b>:1; Mark <b>1</b>:21;
<b>6</b>:2; Luke <b>23</b>:56; Acts <b>13</b>:14, 42, 44; <b>16</b>:12</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
<i>Sabbath</i> as a generality or kind of thing: Matthew <b>12</b>:5, 8; Mark <b>2</b>:27<sup>2</sup>,
28; <b>15</b>:42; <b>16</b>:1; Luke <b>6</b>:5; <b>23</b>:54; John <b>5</b>:18;
<b>9</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
<i>a Sabbath</i>: Matthew <b>12</b>:10, 11, 12; <b>24</b>:20; Mark <b>2</b>:23,
24; <b>3</b>:1, 4; Luke <b>4</b>:31;<b> 6</b>:1, 2, 7, 9; <b>13</b>:14<sup>2</sup>,
15, 16; <b>14</b>:1, 3, 5; John<b> 5</b>:9, 16; <b>7</b>:22, 23<sup>2</sup>; <b>9</b>:13,
31; <b>19</b>:31</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sackcloth 
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
by <i>burlap</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>salute/greet  
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>reduced
in number in Paul’s long set of salutations in Romans <b>16</b>:1-24 and
Colossians <b>4</b>:7-17.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>save</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     (a)
reserved for saving from sin (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σῴζω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>heal</i> for diseases, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <i>exorcise</i> for exorcisms</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Savior</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
capitalized throughout the New Testament because always in reference to Jesus
Christ</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(I)
say (unto you)</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    <i>I’m telling you</i> (some thirty
times in <i>CV</i>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>saying</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  Virtually
always omitted as a free-standing participle. The habitual use of <i>saying</i>
ahead of a direct quotation reflects the Hebrew </span><span lang=HE dir=RTL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ל</span><span
lang=HE dir=RTL style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ֵאמֹר</span><span
dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span
dir=LTR></span> as a marker for direct quotations</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>. Translating it
creates a redundancy in English, <i>“He spoke to him, saying.”</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sea                   </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
replaced by <i>lake</i> since the internal bodies of water in Palestine do not
qualify as seas in current English usage: Lake Galilee, Lake Tiberias (</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John
<b>6</b>:1, 23; <b>21</b>:1), Lake Gennesaret (</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>14</b>:34; Mark <b>6</b>:53; Luke <b>5</b>:1). The Dead Sea would meet the
requirements, but the New Testament does not name it.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
called <i>sea</i> when referring to the <u>Mediterranean Sea</u> (Simon the
tanner beside the sea (Acts <b>10</b>:6, 32), in Revelation because it
evidently refers to the Mediterranean Sea, the <u>Red Sea</u> (1 Corinthians <b>10</b>:1,
2), places that mention <u>sand of the sea</u> (Romans<b> 9</b>:27).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Sea
of Galilee   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Lake Galilee: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>4</b>:18; <b>15</b>:29; Mark <b>1</b>:16; 7:31; John <b>6</b>:1; <b>21</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span lang=DA
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Sea
of Gennesaret</span></i><span lang=DA style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   Lake Gennesaret: </span><sup><span
lang=DA style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
lang=DA style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>5</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Sea
of Tiberias</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   Lake Tiberias: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>John
<b>6</b>:1; <b>21</b>:1</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>see</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>       <i>see
again</i> as a possible translation of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀναβλέπω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
in Jesus’ healings of the blind, because they do not all seem to have been born
blind (Mark <b>8</b>:24, <i>“I see men like trees, walking”</i>; cp. Acts <b>9</b>:12,
17, 18; <b>22</b>:13 re the apostle Paul). That assumption plays on the prefix </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀνα</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>-
to mean <i>again</i> rather than (<i>to look</i>) <i>up</i> either to heaven
(Matthew <b>14</b>:19) or up ahead (Mark <b>16</b>:14). The point cannot be
pressed, because <i>seeing </i>again could be called <i>seeing</i> in the sense
of <i>looking up</i>.<i> </i>Besides, </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀναβλέπω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
occurs in the account of the man born blind (John <b>9</b>:11, 15, 18). So, it
is best to rely on context for detecting the difference. That can leave the
matter unresolvable in several cases</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>seek</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     used
only for <i>look for</i>, which often replaces it</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not used if conative <i>try to</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>seize</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    reduced
usage; replaced with <i>grab</i>, <i>arrest</i>, <i>capture</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>-self/selves</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(reflexive pronouns, intensive reflexive pronouns, and intensive-reflexive
adjectives) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) <u>Reflexive
pronouns</u> “reflect” the subject of their clause. English sometimes uses a
simple pronoun if the reference is clear: <i>“You always have poor people with
you</i> [</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἑαυτοῦ</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>]<i>”</i> (Matthew<b> 26</b>:11).
When they are direct objects, <i>–self</i> pronouns come into play
consistently: <i>“I hurt myself.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <u>Intensive
pronouns</u> emphasize the noun they restate, and thereby create a contrast
with parallel possibilities. In <i>CV</i>, intensive pronouns consistently fall
at the end of their clauses, as in “I did it <i>myself</i>” (rather than
immediately after the noun they intensify, <i>“I myself did it.”</i>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) <u>Intensive
reflexive adjectives</u> (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἴδιος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
ideally combine the previous two elements. Vocabulary lists typically add <i>own</i>
to <i>my</i>, <i>you</i>, <i>his</i>, <i>her</i>, and <i>their</i> to
distinguish the English usage from simple possessive. But that addition
intensifies as well as possesses—a feature English often drops. For <i>one’s
own</i>, we have simply said <i>her</i>, <i>etc.</i>: <i>defer to your own
husband</i> becomes <i>defer to your husband</i> (Ephesians <b>5</b>:22; cp. 1
Corinthians <b>14</b>:35; Titus <b>2</b>:5; 1 Peter <b>3</b>:1). <i>Her own</i>
sounds like her husband rather than somebody else’s husband; the writer surely
did not mean that.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>servant   
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>the
translation for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>δοῦλος</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> in a majority of cases.
Practically everybody that works for somebody is called a “slave.” That seems
unlikely. Mark <b>1</b>:20 does speak of <i>“hired servants”</i> that were
working for Zebedee (Mark <b>1</b>:20).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>serve</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    replaced
with <i>wait on</i> when rank is aside from the issue: Peter’s mother-in-law <i>waited
on </i>them right after Jesus healed her (Matthew <b>5</b>:15).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>shall</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
not used; replaced with <i>will</i> or <i>going to</i> for futures indicatives</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
</i>replaced with a command form in cases of the Greek imperatival future</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>she’s</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
contraction for <i>she is</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) sometimes a contraction for <i>she
has</i>: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew <b>26</b>:10;
Mark <b>14</b>:6, 9; Luke <b>7</b>:45; Romans <b>16</b>:2</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ship     </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>reserved
for larger, sea-going vessels; <i>boat</i> used for smaller craft as on Lake
Galilee</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sir        See
entries above under<i> L</i></span><i><span style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sit/sat</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  In
place of <i>sit down</i> or <i>sat down</i>, <i>CV</i> has used <i>reclined at
table</i>, because the customary eating position seems to be resting in at
least semi-prone position on “couches.” The custom shows through when John
leaned back on Jesus’ chest at the Last Supper to ask who the betrayer was
(John <b>13</b>:25).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sky</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>       instead
of <i>heaven</i> unless apparently referring to God’s dwelling place</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>slave</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    usually
rendered <i>servant</i> (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>δοῦλος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
to remove some of the harshness in the word <i>slave</i>. The term occurs so
often, we wonder whether it carries a broader reference in the New Testament. <i>CV
</i>keeps <i>slave</i> in Colossians <b>3</b>:11; Revelation <b>18</b>:13.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sleep</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
translated <i>die</i>/<i>death</i> when used euphemistically for <u>death </u></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
asleep</i> replaces the adjective <i>dead</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>so</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                    (a)
one way of indicating <u>purpose</u> (along with simple infinitives): <i>“I’ve
made myself a servant to everybody so I can win more of them”</i> (1
Corinthians <b>9</b>:19). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) one way of
indicating <u>result</u> (along with </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>εἰς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τὸ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>infinitive)
either with an infinitive or the indicative. The classical distinction between
tendential result (<i>so as to</i>) and actual result (<i>so that</i>) does not
hold well in the New Testament. The actual-result formula appears in about
twenty places, including Matthew <b>19</b>:6: <i>“ . . . so they’re no longer
two but one”</i> (= Mark <b>10</b>:8). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The tendential
formula, the majority usage, appears in Mark <b>1</b>:45: <i>“ . . . so he was
no longer able to go into a town openly.”</i> If we maintain the tendential
distinction here, the statement means <i>“so he tended not to be able to go
into any town openly.”</i> In this passage, we rendered it tendential: <i>“ . .
. so he had a hard time going into a town openly anymore.” </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Some places sound
more like an inference of thought than a result of action: <i>“So don’t take
pride in people”</i> (1 Corinthians <b>3</b>:21).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Using <i>so</i> by
itself—without <i>that</i> or <i>as to</i>—leaves the matter unspecified. The
difficulty there is that a typical English reader would probably not have
reason to think about the actual-tendential distinction.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Punctuation with <i>so
</i>can be complicated and indefinite. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(1) <i>CV </i>does
not usually place a comma ahead of <i>so </i>when it introduces a purpose
statement, unless the purpose construction is especially long. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(2) When <i>so</i>
introduces a result clause, a comma usually appears before it: Mark <b>1</b>:45;
<b>3</b>:9, 14, 32; <i>etc.</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(3) In longer
instances with <i>so</i> as result, a semicolon separates the clauses: John <b>12</b>:50;
Acts <b>16</b>:3; <b>20</b>:3, <i>etc.</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(4) If the break
before the result seems significant, a period precedes the clause and <i>So </i>is
capitalized in the next sentence: Hebrews <b>4</b>:14; <b>10</b>:1; <b>11</b>:16,
<i>etc.</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(5) With the feel
of an even greater break, there may be a period and <i>So</i> followed by a
comma as a kind of replacement for <i>therefore</i>: Matthew<b> 22</b>:28; <b>25</b>:13;
Acts <b>2</b>:30; <b>19</b>:13; <b>26</b>:19; Romans <b>3</b>:1; <b>5</b>:12; <b>6</b>:21;
<b>7</b>:4, 13; <b>8</b>:12; <b>11</b>:11; <b>15</b>:19; `1 Corinthians<b> 3</b>:21;<b>
4</b>:5; <b>7</b>:33; <b>8</b>:4;<b> 14</b>:39; 2 Corinthians<b> 4</b>:1;
Galatians <b>3</b>:19, 21; <b>4</b>:16; Ephesians <b>2</b>:11; Philippians <b>2</b>:1,
12; <b>3</b>:1;<b> 4</b>:1; 2 Thessalonians<b> 2</b>:15; Hebrews <b>3</b>:7; 1
Peter<b> 1</b>:21<b>; 2</b>:1, 9. On occasion, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(6) <i>so</i> is
omitted in the purpose-result complex: “<i>they’re no longer two but one” </i>(Mark
<b>8</b>:10). The rationale is the same as for omitting <i>because </i>when the
purpose-result is obvious without statement.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>someone</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <i>somebody  
Somebody</i> appears in less formal circumstances. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Son</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      (a)
capitalized in reference to Jesus; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) lower case for other references</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>son
of man</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>   <i>a person</i>; reference to a typical person:
Matthew <b>12</b>:8, <i>“A person is more important than the Sabbath” </i>or <i>“A
person takes precedence over Sabbath”</i> instead of <i>“The Son of Man is Lord
of the Sabbath.”</i> Taken s a reference to Jesus would, of course, work  too.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Son
of Man</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>   as a reference to Jesus capitalizes both nouns:
Matthew <b>24</b>:30, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sons</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
   when not referring to biological sons, rendered<i> children </i>in the
interests of inclusive language: Matthew <b>5</b>:9; Luke <b>16</b>:8, Galatians
<b>4</b>:5, 6, 7, 28, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sons
of   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) replaced by<i> descendants of</i> when not
referring to immediate offspring;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (b) <i>like</i>
when covering a descriptive genitive: Matthew<b> 23</b>:31; Luke <b>6</b>:35;
Colossians <b>3</b>:6</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (c) <i>participants
in</i> (the resurrection): Luke <b>20</b>:36</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>sound</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
the translation for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>φωνή</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, when not
referring to a person; <i>voice, </i>when a person is making the sound.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>spirit/Spirit  
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
capitalized for deity, that is, when classed with Father and Son, especially
when combine with <i>Holy</i>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) <i>CV</i> has
reduced <i>Spirit</i> to <i>spirit</i> in several cases involving descriptive
genitive and the like:      </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when contrasted to
flesh (John <b>3</b>:5-7; Romans<b> 8</b>:4; Galatians <b>5</b>:16-24;
Philippians <b>3</b>:3; Ephesians <b>6</b>:17 in context; 1 Timothy <b>3</b>:16
<i>e.g</i>.)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when in contrast
to other parts of a human being: body, soul, and spirit (1 Thessalonians<b> 5</b>:23)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        when
referring to angels (Hebrews <b>1</b>:7)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        when
referring to people in the intermediate state (1 Peter <b>3</b>:19)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        when
<i>vs</i>. <i>letter</i> referring to the intended meaning of scripture (Romans
<b>2</b>:29; <b>7</b>:6; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>2 Corinthians <b>3</b>:6<sup>2</sup>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when in reference
to evil spirits, unclean spirits, demons that were exorcised: Matthew <b>8</b>:16;
<b>10</b>:1; <b>12</b>:28, <i>etc.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when seeming to
indicate the attitude Christians have that comes from God’s influence in us: <i>“We
know he’s in us by the spirit he’s given us”</i> (1 John <b>3</b>:24, for
example); note as well our rendering of the textual variant in Luke <b>5</b>:55b:
<i>“you don’t know what mentality/attitude you’re supposed to have.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            The
Greek word </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πνεῦμα</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>also
means (c) <i>wind</i> (John <b>3</b>:8; Hebrews <b>1</b>:7) and (d) <i>breath</i>
(Matthew <b>27</b>:50; 2 Thessalonians <b>2</b>:8; cp. the verb in John <b>20</b>:22
(<i>blew</i>). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>steward</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   property
manager<i>  </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>stoicheia</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
<i>typical understandings</i>, <i>basic beliefs</i>, <i>fundamentals, elements </i>(</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>στοιχεῖα</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>straightway   
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced
with <i>right away</i>, <i>immediately</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;
text-indent:-40.3pt'><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>submit to           </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
<i>Defer to</i> has been our rendering in the household teaching material
(Ephesians <b>5</b>:22-33; Colossians <b>3</b>:18-25; 1 Peter<b> 2</b>:18-<b>3</b>:7)
and characteristics lists (1 Timothy <b>3</b>:1-7, 8-13; <b>5</b>:5-10. It
better indicates the attitude and behavior people take with someone else they
know is being held responsible (“head”) for the work involved. Besides, <i>submit</i>
has picked up a negative connotation present in response to bullying. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Less intense, <i>cooperate</i>
seems right for 1 Corinthians <b>16</b>:16. “Cooperating” with people like the
household of Stephanas in ministry seems more likely Paul’s point. There is no
indication Stephanas’ household had some authoritative or directive role over
the Corinthians. If people willingly volunteer themselves in ministry, those
around them with less involvement should do what they can to help. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>suffer
  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)
used for painful experiences</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) otherwise replaced by <i>let</i>,<i>
allow</i>: Matthew <b>19</b>:14</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>talk
with</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
replaced with <i>talk to</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>testify/testimony</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
<i>CV </i>attempts to replace some of the many uses of </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μαρτυρέω</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>/</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>μαρτύριον</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>when
it means merely <i>to speak on behalf of</i>. Current English usage associates
testifying and testimony with courtroom settings. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) <i>speak </i>(Matthew <b>23</b>:31;
Mark<b> 13</b>:4, <i>etc.</i>); </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>speak for </i>me (Luke <b>21</b>:13, <i>etc.</i>);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (c) <i>speak
to the fact that</i> (John<b> 7</b>:7; 2 Corinthians<b> 8</b>:3; 1 John <b>4</b>:14).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>than</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
             (a) used colloquially as a preposition: </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>11</b>:22 (“<i>stronger than him”</i>); Matthew <b>3</b>:11 (<i>“greater
than me”</i>); <i>“greater than him”</i> (Matthew <b>11</b>:11).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) otherwise
treated as a conjunction, that is, using the same case after as the parallel
element before </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>that
                 </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) usually used for aforesaid
demonstratives even when Greek has the near demonstrative for <i><u>this/these</u></i>.
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) Once the item
of discussion is on the table, <i>that</i> rather than <i>this</i> can usually
become the demonstrative for it: 1 Corinthians <b>12</b>:11; <b>13</b>:13.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)
<i>That</i>, for translating the Greek </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὅτι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
is omitted for introducing indirect discourse, that is, for constructions that
purport to give someone’s <u>idea</u> rather than the <u>actual words</u> in
expressing it. The construction comes after leading verbs of saying, the
senses, or mental action: John<b> 18</b>:34, <i>etc.</i>, very often. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>In New Testament
Greek, the </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὅτι</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> conjunction appears with
direct discourse as well. Under both circumstances we have dropped the <i>that</i>.
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (d)
omitted if covering a relative pronoun for the direct object inside a relative
clause: <i>“I love the picture <s>that</s> you sent me.”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        We
have endeavored to keep from having too many <i>that’s</i> close together.  <i>That</i>
can be a demonstrative, a conjunction introducing indirect discourse, purpose
clauses, and fear clauses; or it can be a relative pronoun. So, more than one
of them can come close to each other. For example, Matthew <b>3</b>:8-11 could
read, </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“</span><i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Who warned you to
flee from God’s fury <u>that</u>’s coming? </span></i><b><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>8</span></sup></b><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Bear
fruit <u><sup>that</sup></u><sup>’s</sup> appropriate to repentance. </span></i><b><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>9</span></sup></b><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Don’t
think, ‘Abraham’s our father.’ From these rocks God can raise descendants of
Abraham. </span></i><b><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>10</span></sup></b><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>An
axe is already lying at the base of the trees. Every tree <u>that</u> doesn’t
bear good fruit will be chopped down and thrown in the fire. </span></i><b><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>11</span></sup></b><i><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>I’m</span></u></i><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> immersing
you in water to repentance. The One <u><sup>that</sup></u><sup>’s </sup>who’s
coming after me is greater than me.”</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><i><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Some
of them can be omitted; others can be changed to <i>who.</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>that
which</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>  not used; replaced by <i>what</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>the
                  </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a)<i> </i>usually<i> </i>covers the Greek
article</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
Greek article sometimes replaced with an English possessive adjective: <i>his</i>,
<i>her</i>, <i>their</i>, <i>etc.</i> Greek is often content to use an article
where English wants to specify the possessor even if that is obvious: Romans <b>7</b>:25;
1 Corinthians<b> 4</b>:19; <b>15</b>:25; <b>16</b>:12; 1 Timothy <b>1</b>:16.
It is not that the Greek article <u>means</u> possessive adjective, but that
Greek idiom is satisfied to use an article by custom in places where English
wants to specify a possessive pronoun.                      </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (c)
Sometimes we have used neither <i>the</i> nor <i>a</i> where the Greek article
appears. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>SPECIAL NOTE. The
Greek article marks <u>contrast/identity</u>; the absence of the article marks <u>quality</u>.
It does not indicate definiteness particularly, as <i>the</i> does in English.
Its absence draws attention to the characteristics/qualities/nature that the
referent has. Its presence just refers to it, period—as in distinction from
another parallel thing, period. For example, we have translated John <b>1</b>:17,
<i>“Law came through Moses; grace and truth came through Jesus Christ”</i> (</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ὁ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>νόμος</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>διὰ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Μωϋσέως</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐδόθην</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἡ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>χάρις</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>καὶ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἡ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἀληθεῖα</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>διὰ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Ἰησοῦς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Χριστὸς</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἐγένετο</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>).
That rendering understands the passages as contrasting the kind of thing law is
and the kind of thing grace-and-truth is. Putting <i>the </i>with <i>law</i>
would make it mean the Law of Moses as distinguished from some other law or
thing. Putting <i>the</i> with <i>grace</i> or <i>truth</i> does not “sound
right” (because they are not definite, but kinds of things, abstractions); yet
Greek has articles on both as well as on <i>law</i>. Generic reference is the
reason <i>CV </i>omits the English definite article in some high-profile cases;
<i>“<u>I’m</u> resurrection and life”</i> (John <b>11</b>:25); <i>“<u>I’m</u>
the way, truth, and life”</i> (John <b>14</b>:6).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:.5in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:1.0in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            The Greek article <i>vs</i>.
no article cannot correspond to the English definite article, indefinite
article, and no article; two cannot readily correspond with three. English uses
<i>the</i> to identify one example <i>vs</i>. other examples in the group
(definite/identity). <i>A</i> indicates any example in the group; it does not
matter which one (indefinite identity). In English, the difference is between
definite and indefinite. The lack of either kind of English article<i> </i>means<i>
</i>quality, that is, a kind of thing. A complicating factor in English is that
<i>a </i>can also be used with non-abstractions to mean quality too or a noun
typical of its class: <i>“A dog is a man’s best friend.”</i> The point is not
that the dog is indefinite (<i>“any dog will do”</i>). The point is that the
kind of thing a dog is makes it a best friend for the kind of thing a man is!
The <i>a</i> moves the non-abstraction into an abstraction.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>this</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      We
have somewhat reduced the number of demonstrative pronouns, replacing them with
personal pronouns: Matthew <b>11</b>:7; Luke <b>19</b>:40.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>this
day</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
today</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>this
night</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>   tonight</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>those</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> sometimes
replaced with <i>the</i> <i>one(s</i>) or <i>people </i>as a translation of an
articular participle; they are translations when <i>those</i> would not be a
demonstrative pronoun or adjective</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>those
who</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
  frequently becomes <i>the ones that</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>thence</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>there</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    avoided
as an expletive (<i>“There’s a bat in the attic.”</i>); used only as an adverb
for location</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>therein</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>this/these</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   reserved
for an <u>upcoming</u> demonstrative; <i>that/those</i> used for <u>aforesaid</u>
references</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>tithe</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
replaced with </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>“give a tenth”</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
Matthew <b>23</b>:23; Luke<b> 19</b>:12; <b>11</b>:42</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>thither</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>thereupon</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>therefore</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  replaced
with <i>so</i>; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>frequently omitted whether
translating </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἄρα</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>, </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γάρ</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>διὰ</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>τοῦτο</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>διότι</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>οὖν</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
or </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>τοίνυν</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
