style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>they</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     sometimes
used advisedly, that is, as an indefinite pronoun equal to <i>people (say)</i>:
Matthew<b> 5</b>:16; Acts<b> 10</b>:47 </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>thief</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     for
the men crucified with Jesus, see under <i>insurrectionist </i>above</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>those</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    used
as a plural distant demonstrative and infrequently as equal to <i>the ones</i>,
that is, to translate a plural articular substantive participle</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>tomb</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    for
a burial chamber erected above ground or dug into a hillside; <u>grave</u> for
burial in the ground</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>transgression</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   
replaced with <i>sin</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>tribulation</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
replaced usually with <i>hardship</i>, <i>suffering, ordeal</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>truly</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    omitted
as an equivalent for <i>“verily”</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>unbelief</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
replaced by <i>dis</i>belief if the text is dealing with a person that has
heard the message </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Uncircumcision</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   capitalized
as a designation for the Gentiles: </span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Romans
<b>3</b>:30; Ephesians<b> 2</b>:11</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>unquenchable
fire</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
replaced with <i>a fire you can’t put out</i>: Matthew<b> 3</b>:12; Luke <b>3</b>:17</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>unto     </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not
used; replaced with <i>to</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>upon    </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>not
used; replaced with <i>on</i> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>verily
(verily) I say to you</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> The <i>verily</i> is dropped completely.
The <i>I say to you</i> becomes <i>I tell you</i>. The whole expression falls
from the text except for perhaps once a chapter, where the shorter expression
suffices.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>very
</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>often
eliminated to accommodate English preference for expressive restraint: Matthew <b>4</b>:8;
Luke <b>19</b>:17; 1 Corinthians <b>6</b>:11; 2 Corinthians <b>8</b>:24.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>village</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
the translation for </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κώμη</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>. <i>Town</i> and <i>city
</i>translate </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>πόλις</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>—<i>town</i> when designating
an urban area that does not seem to qualify as a <i>city</i> in the modern
sense. See <i>city</i> above.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>voice
               </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) used only for human audible expression
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i> </i>replaced
with <i>sound</i> in passages like 1 Corinthians <b>14</b>:10-11 that refer to
other than human audible expression</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c)<i>
</i>dropped<i> </i>altogether in phrases like <i>hear the Son of Man</i>, which
shortens, <i>hear the voice of the Son of Man. </i>That wording eliminates the
body-part aspect of the original.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>walk</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                (a)
reserved almost exclusively for physically walking</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
replaced by <i>live/living</i> when figurative for conducting life: Romans <b>13</b>:13;
2 Corinthians <b>10</b>:2, 3; Ephesians <b>2</b>:2; 1 John <b>2</b>:6, 7; 2
John 4, 6; 3 John 3; Revelation <b>3</b>:4; <b>21</b>:24</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>we</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>        Galatians
<b>6</b>:7-8 substitutes <i>we</i> for “a man” as a kind of advised usage of <i>we</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>weep/wept</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
replaced by <i>cry</i>, even <i>sob</i> as when Peter <i>“broke down”</i> after
his denials (Luke<b> 22</b>:62)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>What
have ___ to do with you?</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <i>What’s between __ and __:</i> <i>What
to me and to you? </i>Possible ways of translating a Hebrew idiom in the
gospels, which we have rephrased as <i>What <u>is</u> this? </i>(</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew<b>
8</b>:29; Mark<b> 1</b>:24; <b>5</b>:7; Luke<b> 4</b>:34; <b>8</b>:28; John<b>
2</b>:4)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>whence</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
  not used—along with <i>hither</i>, <i>thither</i>, <i>hence</i>, <i>thence</i>
as out-of-date directionals</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>wherein</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   not
used</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>whereupon</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   not
used </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>whether</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> kept
for statements of alternatives between real options: Romans <b>4</b>:16; <b>14</b>:8;
1 Corinthians <b>10</b>:31; <b>12</b>:13; 2 Corinthians <b>5</b>:9, 13<sup>2</sup>;
<b>7</b>:3; <b>12</b>:2; Ephesians <b>6</b>:8; Philippians <b>1</b>:18, 20, 27;<b>
2</b>:12; 1 Thessalonians<b> 5</b>:10; 1 John <b>4</b>:1, 2; <b>5</b>:2. <i>If</i>
addresses positive <i>vs</i>. negative as in the case of an introduction to
indirect questions: <i>“He asked if he could borrow the car” </i>(cp. Matthew <b>26</b>:63,
<i>etc.</i>; see comments under <i>if</i> above). </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>who</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>     avoided
almost entirely; replaced with <i>that</i> for relative pronouns for persons</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>whom</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  never
used because of its pedantic feel; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(a) </span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>who</span></u><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
replaces <i>whom </i>even when standard grammar calls for <i>whom</i>: Luke <b>11</b>:19;
<b>12</b>:5; John <b>6</b>:68; <b>13</b>:18, 22, 24; <b>18</b>:4, 7;<b> 20</b>:15;
2 Corinthians <b>10</b>:18.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)
<i>Who</i> is used to create variety in John <b>5</b>:24.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(four)
winds</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>   every direction (Matthew<b> 24</b>:31) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>wise</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> 
sometimes replaced by <i>smart</i> to translate </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>σόφος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>:
</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>7</b>:24; <b>24</b>:45; Luke <b>16</b>:8; Romans <b>1</b>:22; <b>12</b>:16;
1 Corinthians <b>6</b>:5; <b>10</b>:15; 2 Corinthians <b>11</b>:19</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>woman</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
(a) used only outside the vocative; </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b) omitted (</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke
<b>22</b>:57; John <b>2</b>:4; <b>4</b>:21; [[<b>8</b>:10]]; <b>19</b>:26; <b>20</b>:15)
</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(c) translated <i>dear woman</i> (</span><sup><span
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Matthew
<b>15</b>:28; Luke <b>13</b>:12; John <b>20</b>:13).<i> </i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify'><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>As
a word of direct address, <i>woman</i> has a negative connotation in English that
does not fit any of the vocative uses of </span><span lang=EL style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γυνή</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>in
the New Testament (</span><span lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γύναι</span><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>). At first, when
we included it, we rendered it <i>ma’am</i>, but<i> dear woman </i>seemed to be
a better option.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(from
the) womb</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'> adjusted to <i>from birth</i>, as part of the shift
away from body-part language (Luke <b>1</b>:15) or used circumlocution (Luke <b>1</b>:44);
elsewhere retained as imbedded idiom (Luke <b>11</b>:27; <b>23</b>:29; John <b>3</b>:4).</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>word</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
<i>word</i>, an individual word</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (b)
<i>message</i>, frequently when not referring to an individual word</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>work</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>    (a)
something that a person <i>does</i>, a <i>deed</i> (James 2)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            (b)
something that <i>produces</i> a result <i>vs</i>. something bestowed by
another, like righteousness that God considers a person as having. This second
usage predominates in Romans and Galatians with respect to salvation theory:
note Romans <b>4</b>:4-5, <i>e.g</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>world</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>   (a)
an English term sometimes omitted as overly “broad-scoped” (2 Corinthians <b>1</b>:14);</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(b)<i>
empire</i>, when the Roman empire—the territory around the Mediterranean Sea—is
the apparent reference (</span><sup><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:
115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>+</span></sup><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Luke <b>2</b>:1;
Acts <b>11</b>:28; <b>17</b>:6; <b>24</b>:5)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>worship</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>           (a)
<i>worship</i>, when directed toward deity (</span><span lang=HE dir=RTL
style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>עבד
</span><span dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:14.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span dir=LTR></span>, <span lang=HE
dir=RTL>שׁבד </span><span dir=LTR></span><span dir=LTR></span>, <span lang=HE
dir=RTL>שׁחה</span></span><span dir=LTR></span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><span dir=LTR></span>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                        (b)
<i>pay homage to, bow down to</i>, when applied to other than deity</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><span style='font-size:
12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            In
occasions that involve Jesus, choosing between <i>worship</i> and <i>paying
homage to </i>makes a translator decide whether a person recognized him as
deity. The choice depends on what understanding the person had; the viewpoint
of the translator/reader would otherwise project himself into the text. So, the
actual text presented in <i>CV</i> is tentative. The only reason for getting
into such decisions at all is that <i>worship</i> in English has specialized
its meaning as directed to deity. Bowing down in homage to another human being
has fallen out of western culture as an expression of respect or homage. So the
English term does not have the second application that </span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>προσκυνέω</span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
</span><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>had.
In everyday speech, <i>worship </i>sometimes describes exaggerated respect for
someone (<i>“He worshipped the very ground she walked on.”</i>), but that does
not come up in the biblical text. So, <i>worship</i> and <i>lord</i> put a
translator in the awkward position the <i>Revised Standard Version</i> brought
into gospels when it used <i>thou</i> for deity and <i>you</i> for other
references.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(is)
worthy (of)   </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>replaced by <i>deserves, considered
appropriate for, good enough for</i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>wrath</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>  
an outmoded word replaced by <i>anger</i>, <i>rage</i>, <i>fury</i>; <i>displeasure</i>
(Colossians <b>3</b>:6)</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(is)
written </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>switched to anarthrous <i>scripture says</i> for </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>γέγραπται</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
to avoid passive voice. The phrasing assumes a stative value for the passive
perfect here (<i>it stands written</i>) and uses a simple present to cover the
original wording.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>wrote   </span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>shifted
often to </span><i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>have written </span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>(</span><span lang=EL
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ἔγραψα</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>)
to leave the possibility for epistolary aorist (2 Corinthians<b> 5</b>:9; 1
John <b>2</b>:14), epistolary aorist meaning a simple past-tense verb used in
reference to the same writing in which it appears. The custom grew out of the
greater time distance the slow postal system had in those bygone centuries; by
the time the recipient got the letter, some time had passed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Yahveh</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
not used in the original Greek New Testament or New Testament quotations from
the Old Testament. Its Old Testament quotations follow the Septuagint, where </span><span
lang=EL style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>κύριος</span><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>,
<i>Lord</i>, replaces God’s personal name in the Hebrew text.  See statistics
under <i>L</i></span><i><span style='font-size:9.0pt;line-height:115%;
font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>ORD</span></i><span style='font-size:12.0pt;
line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> above.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:0in;
margin-left:.5in;text-align:justify;text-indent:-.5in'><i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>you</span></i><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>      sometimes
used advisedly, that is, as an indefinite pronoun: 2 Corinthians <b>4</b>:18; <b>12</b>:4;
1 Timothy<b> 6</b>:16</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><b><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            A
sizeable set of English words currently appear mostly in religious contexts and
with religious connotations—sometimes negative ones. It is difficult to find accurate
and authentic-sounding, modern replacements for Bible words like <i>Almighty</i>,
<i>beget</i>, <i>bless(ed/ness)</i>, <i>confession</i>, <i>defile</i>, <i>the
elect</i>, <i>faith</i>, <i>fellowship</i>, <i>flesh</i>, <i>fulfill</i>, <i>glory</i>,
<i>godly</i>, <i>gospel</i>, <i>heaven</i> (for sky), <i>holy/holiness</i>, <i>iniquity</i>,
<i>joy</i>, <i>persecution</i>, <i>preach</i>, <i>proclaim</i>, <i>prophesy/prophecy</i>,
<i>rejoice</i>, <i>repent/ance</i>, righteous/ness, <i>redeemer</i>, <i>remission</i>,
<i>salvation/save/savior</i>, <i>sanctify</i>, <i>sin/sinner/sinful/sinless</i>,
<i>testify</i> outside of courtroom proceedings, <i>tongue</i> (for language), <i>transgression</i>,
<i>tribulation</i>, <i>voice</i> (for sound), <i>witness</i> outside of court
proceedings, <i>worship</i>, <i>wrath</i>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>            The
notations above indicate two major goals in the <i>Conversational Version. </i>The
first is to express biblical content in conversational usage. The second is to
reduce the wordiness of Hebraic idiom by several shortening mechanisms
scattered throughout the explanations here. Hopefully the desired effect has
been achieved, and the biblical message comes fresh to today’s readers of the
everlasting message.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0in;text-align:justify'><span
style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>                                                                                                                                         
</span><span style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>christir.org</span></p>

style='font-size:12.0pt;line-height:115%;font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>&nbsp;</span></p>
